كتاب الطلاق باب الكنايات في الطلاق والصريح يلحق الصريح والبائن يلحق الصريح لا البائن إلا إذا كان معلقاً بأن نكاح بيننا يقع الطلاق والأصل أن نفي النكاح أصلاً لا يكون طلاقاً بل يكون جحوداً، أنه ونفي النكاح في الحال يكون طلاقاً إذا نوى، وما عداه فالصحيح على هذا الخلاف . قيد بالنية لأنه لا يقع بدون النية اتفاقاً لكونه من الكنايات ولا يخفى أن دلالة الحال تقوم مقامها حيث لم يصلح للرد والشتم ويصلح للجواب فقط . وقدمنا أن الصالح للجواب فقط ثلاثة ألفاظ ليس هذا منها فلذا شرط النية للإشارة إلى أن دلالة الحال هنا لا تكفي. وأشار بقوله «تطلق» إلى أن الواقع بهذه الكناية رجعي. وقيدنا بظهور النكاح لأنه لو قال ما أنت لي بزوجة وأنت طالق لا يكون إقراراً بالنكاح لقيام القرينة المتقدمة على أنه ما أراد بالطلاق حقيقته كما في البزازية أول كتاب النكاح فالنفي لا يقع به بالأولى قوله : (والصريح يلحق الصريح والبائن) فلو قال لها أنت طالق ثم قال أنت طالق أو طلقها على مال وقع الثاني، وكذا لو قال لها أنت بائن أو خالعها على مال ثم قال لها أنت طالق أو هذه طالق كما في البزازية : يقع عندنا لحديث الخدري مسنداً المختلعة يلحقها صريح الطلاق ما دامت في العدة، ولما ذكر في الأصول من بحث الخاص. أطلقه فشمل المنجز والمعلق إذا وجد شرطه، فكما يقع في العدة منجزاً يقع إذا وجد شرطه فيها. وأما إذا علقه في العدة فإنه يصح في جميع الصور إلا إذا كان الطلاق بائناً . ، ثم علق البائن في العدة فإنه غير صحيح اعتباراً بتنجيزه كما في البدائع . قيدنا الصريح اللاحق للبائن بكونه خاطبها به، أو أشار إليها للاحتراز عما إذا قال كل امرأة له طالق فإنه لا يقع على المختلعة وكذا إذا قال إن فعلت كذا فامرأته كذا لا يقع على المعتدة من بائن كما في البزازية والمراد بالصريح هنا ما وقع به الرجعي فتدخل الكنايات الرواجع من اعتدي واستبري رحمك وأنت واحدة وما ألحق بالثلاثة، فلو أبانها أو العدة قال لها في اعتدي ناوياً وقع الثاني في ظاهر الرواية خلافاً لما روي عن أبي يوسف نظراً إلى أنها كناية وجه ظاهر الرواية أن الواقع بها رجعي فكان في معنى الصريح قوله: (وقيدنا بظهور النكاح اعترضه في النهر بأن قول المصنف وتطلق» مستغن عن التقييد به ما في البزازية لو قالت أنا امرأتك فقال لها أنت طالق كان إقراراً بالنكاح وتطلق لاقتضاء الطلاق النكاح وضعاً قوله : : (فإنه لا يقع على (المختلعة أي إلا أن يعنيها فإن عناها طلقت. كذا في كافي الحاكم الشهيد من باب الخلع ا هـ . والظاهر أن عدم الوقوع لكونها ليست امرأة له من كل وجه بل من بعض الأوجه ولذا يقع عليها بالنية بخلاف ما إذا لم ينو لكونها كالأجنبية ولذا قال في حاوي الزاهدي : قال لامرأته أنت طالق واحدة ثم قال إن كنت امرأة لي فأنت طالق ثلاثاً إن كان الطلاق الأول بائناً لا يقع الثاني، وإن كان رجعياً يقع الثاني قوله : محمول على رواية أبي يوسف) أقول : صرح بذلك في كافي الحاكم بعد ذكره ما هو ظاهر الرواية حيث قال : وكذلك لو قال لها بعد الخلع اهـ كما في البدائع، وما في الظهيرية لو قال لها أنت بائن ناوياً الطلاق ثم قال لها في العدة اعتدي أو استبري رحمك أو أنت واحدة ناوياً الطلاق لا يقع، وإن كان الرجعي يلحق البائن محمول على رواية أبي يوسف لكن يرد عليه الطلاق الثالث فإنه من قبيل الصريح اللاحق لصريح وبائن كما في فتح القدير وهي حادثة حلب، وكذا يرد الطلاق على مال بعد البائن فإنه واقع ولا يلزم المال كما في الخلاصة فالأولى إبقاء الصريح في كلامه على حقيقته فيدخل الطلاق الثلاث والطلاق على مال بناء على أن الصريح شامل للبائن والرجعي كما في فتح القدير. وتلحق الكنايات الرواجع به في حق هذا الحكم، وحينئذ فكلامه شامل لما إذا كان الصريح موصوفاً بما يدل على البينونة كأنت طالق بائن بعد أنت بائن فإنه يلحق صريح لحق بائناً، وإن كان بائناً بإلغاء الوصف كما في المحيط والبزازية. لكن يشكل عليه ما في القنية معزياً إلى نظم الزندوستي فيمن قال لمختلعته أو مبانته أنت طالق بائن أو أنت طالق البتة ونوى الثلاث قال أبو يوسف : هي ثلاث خلافاً لزفر فإنه واحدة عنده ا هـ . لأنه اعتدي يريد به الطلاق وقعت عليها تطليقة أخرى لأن اعتدي لا يكون بائناً ولا يراد به الفرقة ولا فساد النكاح. قال أبو الفضل أبو يوسف في موضع آخر : لا يقع بـ«اعتدي على البائنة شيء ا هـ . قوله : لكن يرد عليه الخ) أي على قوله والمراد بالصريح هنا الواقع به الرجعي قوله : (بناء على أن الصريح شامل للبائن والرجعي ولذا فسره في الفتح بأنه ما لا يحتاج إلى نية بائناً كان الواقع به أو رجعياً، ويرد عليه كما في النهر ما مر عن ظاهر الرواية من أنه لو أبانها ثم قال لها في العدة اعتدي ينوي الطلاق أنه يقع إلا أن يجاب عنه بما مر عن البدائع قوله : (لكن) يشكل عليه ما في القنية الخ) أي يشكل على إلغاء الوصف أقول : وذكر صاحب القنية في كتابه الحاوي أيضاً هذه المسألة وعبارته : قال لمختلعته أو لمبانته أنت طالق بائن لا يقع ولو قال أنت طالق البتة ونوى الثلاث لا يقع عند أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف : هي ثلاث خلافاً لزفر فإنه واحدة عنده ا هـ. وما عزاه للإمام أبي حنيفة من عدم الوقوع موافق لما قرره المؤلف عند قول المتن أنت طالق واحدة أولاً الخ» من أن الوصف متى قرن بالعدد كان الوقوع بالعدد وكذا الوقوع بالمصدر عند ذكره. وكذا الوقوع بالصفة عند ذكرها كما إذا قال أنت طالق البتة كان الوقوع بالبتة حتى لو قال بعدها إن شاء الله متصلاً لا يقع ولو كان الوقوع باسم الفاعل لوقع ا أي لأن الوصف يصير فاصلاً بينه وبين الاستثناء، وعلى هذا فإذا كان الوقوع بالوصف وهو هنا لفظ بائن كان من البائن بعد البائن لا من الصريح الواقع به البائن لكن يشكل عليه أنه لا يحتاج إلى النية في أنت طالق بائن فيصدق عليه تعريف الصريح إلا أن يجاب بأن عدم احتياجه إلى النية لدلالة الحال وهي ذكر الطلاق الموصوف بلفظ بائن والدلالة قائمة مقام النية فلم يدخل في تعريف الصريح لأنه متوقف على الدلالة القائمة مقام النية فكأنه توقف على النية وعلى هذا فلا حاجة إلى دعوى إلغاء الوصفية تأمل . هـ.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Allusions (Kinayat) in Divorce. The explicit (sarih) follows the explicit, and the irrevocable (bain) follows the explicit, not the irrevocable, except if suspended, such that marriage between us falls divorce. The principle is that negation of marriage originally is not divorce but denial. Negation of marriage in the present is divorce if intended. And other than that, the correct is based on this difference. It is restricted by intention because it does not occur without intention by agreement, being from allusions. And it is not hidden that contextual indication stands in its place where it is not suitable for rejection and insult and is only suitable for answer. And we previously stated that the words suitable for answer only are three words, and this is not among them, so intention is required to indicate that contextual indication here is not sufficient. And he indicated by his saying 'tutallaq' that what occurs by this allusion is revocable (raj'i). And we restricted by the appearance of marriage because if he said 'You are not a wife to me' and 'You are divorced', it is not an acknowledgment of marriage due to the preceding context that he did not intend the reality of divorce, as in al-Bazzaziyya at the beginning of the Book of Marriage, so negation does not occur with it a fortiori. His saying: (And the explicit follows the explicit and the irrevocable) so if he said to her 'You are divorced' then said 'You are divorced' or divorced her for a consideration, the second occurs. Similarly, if he said to her 'You are bain' or divorced her by khul' for a consideration then said 'You are divorced' or 'this one is divorced', it occurs according to us, due to the hadith of al-Khudri transmitted: 'The woman divorced by khul' is followed by explicit divorce as long as she is in the waiting period.' And for what is mentioned in the principles from the discussion of the specific. He made it absolute, so it includes the immediate and the suspended if its condition exists. So just as it occurs in the waiting period immediately, it occurs if its condition exists therein. As for if he suspends it in the waiting period, it is valid in all forms except if the divorce was bain. Then if he suspended the bain in the waiting period, it is invalid by analogy to its immediate effect as in al-Bada'i'. We restricted the explicit that follows the bain by his addressing her directly or indicating her, to exclude the case where he says 'Every woman of mine is divorced' for it does not occur on the woman divorced by khul'. Similarly, if he said 'If you do such-and-such, then his wife is such-and-such', it does not occur on the woman in waiting period from a bain divorce, as in al-Bazzaziyya. And the meaning of explicit here is that by which the revocable occurs, so the revocable allusions enter, such as 'i'taddi', 'istabri rahimak', 'anti wahidah', and what is annexed to the three. So if he divorced her bain or during the waiting period said to her in 'i'taddi' intending, the second occurs in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), contrary to what is narrated from Abu Yusuf who considered it an allusion. The reason for the apparent narration is that what occurs by it is revocable, so it is in the meaning of explicit. His saying: (And we restricted by the appearance of marriage) was objected to in al-Nahr by saying that the author's statement 'tutallaq' suffices without this restriction, regarding what is in al-Bazzaziyya: if she said 'I am your wife' and he said 'You are divorced', it is an acknowledgment of marriage and she is divorced because divorce entails marriage by nature. His saying: (It does not occur on the mukhtali'ah) meaning unless he intends her, for if he intends her, she is divorced. So in Kafi al-Hakim al-Shahid from the chapter of khul'. End. The apparent is that non-occurrence is because she is not his wife in every respect but from some respects, so it occurs by intention unlike when he does not intend as she is like a foreign woman. Therefore it is said in Hawi al-Zahidi: He said to his wife 'You are divorced once' then said 'If you are my wife, then you are divorced thrice' - if the first divorce was bain, the second does not occur; if it was revocable, the second occurs. His saying: is carried on the narration of Abu Yusuf. I say: This is explained in Kafi al-Hakim after mentioning what is the apparent narration, where he said: Similarly if he said after khul'. End. As in al-Bada'i', and what is in al-Zahiriyya: if he said to her 'You are bain' intending divorce, then said to her in the waiting period 'i'taddi' or 'istabri rahimak' or 'anti wahidah' intending divorce, it does not occur. However, if the revocable follows the bain, it is carried on the narration of Abu Yusuf. But the third divorce is objected to it, for it is from the category of explicit following explicit and bain, as in Fath al-Qadir, and it is the incident of Halab. Similarly, divorce for consideration after bain occurs and the consideration is not obligatory, as in al-Khulasa. So it is better to keep the explicit in his statement in its reality, so the triple divorce and divorce for consideration enter, based on that explicit includes bain and revocable as in Fath al-Qadir. And the revocable allusions join it in respect of this ruling. Then his statement includes whether the explicit is described by what indicates bain, like 'You are divorced bain' after 'You are bain', for then an explicit follows a bain, even if it was bain by disregarding the description, as in al-Muhit and al-Bazzaziyya. But what is in al-Qunyah, attributed to Nadhm al-Zandustani, is problematic: Whoever said to his mukhtali'ah or mubannah 'You are divorced bain' or 'You are divorced al-batta' and intended three, Abu Yusuf said: It is three, contrary to Zufar, for it is one according to him. End. Because 'i'taddi' by which he intended divorce, another divorce occurs for him because 'i'taddi' is not bain and is not intended for separation or corruption of marriage. Abu al-Fadl Abu Yusuf said in another place: Nothing occurs by 'i'taddi' on the bain woman. End. His saying: (But it is objected to it) means on his statement that the meaning of explicit here is that by which revocable occurs. His saying: (Based on that explicit includes bain and revocable, and therefore it was interpreted in al-Fath as that which does not need intention, whether what occurs by it is bain or revocable, and it is objected to it as in al-Nahr what passed about the apparent narration that if he divorced her bain then said to her in the waiting period 'i'taddi' intending divorce, it occurs. But it can be answered by what passed from al-Bada'i'. His saying: (But) what is in al-Qunyah is problematic) means it is problematic for disregarding the description. I say: The author of al-Qunyah also mentioned this issue in his book al-Hawi, and his phrasing: He said to his mukhtali'ah or mubannah 'You are divorced bain' does not occur. If he said 'You are divorced al-batta' and intended three, it does not occur according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: It is three, contrary to Zufar, for it is one according to him. End. What he attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa of non-occurrence is in agreement with what the author established at the statement of the matn 'You are divorced once first...' that when description is coupled with number, occurrence is by number; similarly occurrence by the verbal noun when mentioned; similarly occurrence by the adjective when mentioned, as when he says 'You are divorced al-batta', occurrence is by al-batta such that if he says afterwards 'if Allah wills' connectedly, it does not occur. If occurrence were by the active participle, it would have occurred. This is because the adjective becomes a separator between it and the exception. On this basis, if occurrence is by the description, which here is the word 'bain', it is from the bain after bain, not from the explicit by which bain occurs. But it is problematic that 'You are divorced bain' does not need intention, so it fits the definition of explicit. Except that it can be answered that its not needing intention is due to contextual indication, which is the mention of divorce described by the word 'bain', and contextual indication stands in place of intention, so it does not enter the definition of explicit because it is dependent on contextual indication that stands in place of intention, so it is as if it depends on intention. On this basis, there is no need to claim disregarding description. Reflect. End.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the chapter of allusions (kinayat) in divorce. The commentator, Imam Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, explains the ruling that explicit divorce words (sarih) follow both explicit and irrevocable (bain) divorces, except when the bain is suspended. The principle is that negation of marriage is not divorce but denial. When a husband says 'You are not my wife' intending divorce, it occurs as divorce according to intention, but if said angrily, it may be denial. The commentary emphasizes that allusions (kinayat) require intention and do not occur without it, unlike explicit words. Contextual indication (dalalat al-hal) can substitute for intention in some cases, but not for the specific allusions mentioned. The commentator then discusses the hadith of al-Khudri which proves that explicit divorce applies to a woman in iddah from khul' (which is bain), and by analogy to any bain divorce. However, the hadith is about a specific case; the general ruling is that explicit divorce follows both revocable and irrevocable divorces immediately or when conditions are met. There is an internal Hanafi dispute: the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) holds that even allusions like 'i'taddi' count as explicit after bain, while Abu Yusuf disagrees, considering them pure allusions. The commentary also addresses the effect of description: if a husband says 'You are divorced bain' after a previous bain divorce, the description may render the second divorce ineffective if it is considered a bain after bain. The case from al-Qunyah presents a dispute among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar regarding a man who says 'You are divorced bain' or 'You are divorced al-batta' intending three divorces. Abu Hanifa holds no divorce occurs, Abu Yusuf says three, Zufar says one. The commentator reconciles Abu Hanifa's view by explaining that when description is attached, the occurrence is by the description, not the word 'divorce', so it becomes a bain after bain which is ineffective. He also addresses the objection that 'anti taliq ba'in' does not need intention, so it should be considered explicit. The response is that its independence from intention is due to contextual indication, which is like intention, so it is not truly explicit. This intricate discussion shows the nuanced approach of Hanafi scholars in determining the effect of divorce pronouncements.

Key Terms
صريح (sarih): Explicit words of divorce that do not require intention, such as 'anti taliq'. In this text, sarih includes both raj'i and bain types.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately without possibility of reconciliation during iddah.
كناية (kinayah): Words that allude to divorce but are not explicit, requiring intention for the divorce to take effect.
رجعي (raj'i): Revocable divorce that allows the husband to take back his wife during the waiting period without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (zahir al-riwayah), if a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced' (sarih) after having already divorced her with a bain divorce, what is the ruling?
A) The second divorce does not occur because the wife is already divorced bain.
B) The second divorce occurs and is valid.
C) The second divorce occurs only if the husband intends it.
D) The second divorce occurs but is considered bain again.

Key Takeaway
Explicit divorce words (sarih) are legally effective even after an irrevocable (bain) divorce during the iddah, but when a description like 'bain' is attached, the occurrence may be by the description, leading to different rulings.

The Ba'in Cannot Follow the Ba'in: The Rule of Report in Divorce Kinayat
Commentary expanding the rule that a ba'in utterance does not take effect if it can be interpreted as a report.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding a ba'in utterance to an already ba'in woman and apply it to various scenarios, distinguishing between cases where it is treated as a report versus a new divorce.

Core Idea
A ba'in utterance to an already ba'in woman does not take effect if it can be interpreted as a report, even with intention.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a nuanced rule in Hanafi divorce law. It addresses the situation where a husband uses an allusive word (kinayah) for irrevocable divorce (ba'in) to a woman who is already irrevocably divorced. The key is whether the utterance can be understood as merely reporting the existing separation rather than initiating a new divorce. The commentator explores various applications and exceptions, distinguishing between explicit and allusive wording, and addressing the role of intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the rule
The passage addresses the situation where a husband says a ba'in utterance (e.g., 'anti ba'in' or 'abantuki') to a woman who is already in a ba'in divorce (mab'anah). The rule is that it does not take effect if the utterance can be interpreted as a report (khabar) about the first divorce.
The basis: the utterance is true as a report, so there is no need to treat it as an initiation (insha').
2
Distinguish between explicit and allusive words
Explicit words like 'taliq' (divorced) take effect even on a mab'anah because they are legally determined for initiation. Allusive words (kinayat) are subject to the report interpretation.
Explicit ba'in words like 'anti taliq ba'in' also take effect because the word 'taliq' remains after canceling 'ba'in'.
3
Analyze the role of intention
If the utterance can be interpreted as a report, the husband's intention to create a second divorce does not make it occur. Intention only matters when the utterance cannot be a report (e.g., when it includes 'another' or when he intends the severe separation).
The relied-upon position is that occurrence does not happen, but some commentators lean towards occurrence if the intention is clear.
4
Apply the exception: suspended (mu'allaq) ba'in
A suspended ba'in (e.g., 'if you enter the house, you are ba'in') does take effect on a mab'anah if the condition occurs after the immediate ba'in, because the suspension is prior and creates a new divorce.
This is the exception mentioned at the end: 'إلا إذا كان معلقاً'.
5
Consider related issues: khul', zihar, li'an, ila', takhyir
The passage extends the principle to other areas. For example, khul' after a ba'in divorce for consideration is not valid because it would obtain what is already obtained (immediate deliverance). Similarly, zihar, li'an, ila', and takhyir are examined to confirm that the mab'anah is not a suitable subject for these rulings.
These extensions reinforce the core idea that a ba'in utterance has no effect on a woman already separated irrevocably.

الثالث ولا يجب المال لأنه إعطاء المال لتحصيل الخلاص المنجز وأنه حاصل، وأما اشتراط قبولها في أول المسألة فلأن قوله أنت طالق على ألف تعليق طلاقها بالقبول فلا يقع بلا وجود الشرط ا هـ . وشمل كلامه ما لو قال للمبانة أبنتك بتطليقة فإنه لا يقع بخلاف أنت طالق بائن كما في البزازية. وفرق في الذخيرة بينهما بأن إذا ألغينا بائناً يبقى قوله «طالق» وبه يقع، ولو ألغينا أبنتك يبقى قوله بتطليقة» وهو غير مفيد. وقيدنا بإمكان كونه خبراً عن الأول لأنه لو لم يمكن بأن نوى بالبائن الثاني البينونة الغليظة قيل يصدق فيما نوى ويقع الثلاث لأنها محل البينونة والحرمة الغليظة وقيل لا يصدق لأن التغليظ صفة للبينونة فإذا ألغت النية في أصل البينونة لكونها حاصلة لغت في إثبات وصف .التغليظ كذا في المحيط. واقتصر الشارحون على الوقوع لكن بصيغة ينبغي فكان الوقوع هو المعتمد. وفي البزازية : لو قال للمبانة أبنتك أخرى يقع لأنه لا يصلح جواباً ا أي لا يصلح كونه خبراً عن الأول. وفي القنية : لو قال لها أنت بائن ثم قال في عدتها أنت بائن بتطليقة أخرى يقع ا وينبغي أنه إذا أبانها ثم قال لها أنت بائن ناوياً طلقة ثانية أن تقع الثانية بنيته لأنه بنيته لا يصلح خبراً فهو كما لو قال أبنتك بأخرى إلا أن يقال إن الوقوع إنما هو بلفظ صالح له وهو أخرى بخلاف مجرد النية. وأشار المؤلف بعدم كون المبانة محلاً للبائن إلى أنها ليست محلاً للظهار واللعان؛ أما الظهار فموجبه الحرمة والحرمة حاصلة بالبينونة، وأما اللعان فهو حكم مشروع في قذف الزوجات والزوجية منقطعة. كذا في المحيط . ولو آلى منها لم يصح إيلاؤه في حكم البر لأنه في حق البر تعليق الإبانة شرعاً، وقيام الملك شرط صحة الإبانة تنجيزاً كان أو تعليقاً كما في التعليق الحقيقي. ولو خيرها في العدة لا يصح بأن قال لها اختاري فاختارت نفسها في العدة لم يقع شيء لأنه تمليك والتمليك بلا ملك لا يتصور. كذا في البدائع. ولا يقال إنه معلق باختيارها فينبغي أن يلحق لأن البائن إذا كان معلقاً يلحق لأنا نقول ليس بمعلق بل هي قائمة مقامه فإيقاعها إيقاع مبتدأ لا أثر لتعليق سابق . قوله : (إلا إذا كان معلقاً)

Al-Khulasa. The Book of Divorce. Chapter on Kinayat in Divorce. His statement: '(not the ba'in)' meaning the ba'in does not follow the ba'in when it is possible to make it a report about the first because it is true, so there is no need to make it a composition. And it is not refuted by 'You are divorced, you are divorced' because there is no probability in it due to its being determined for composition legally, so even if he said 'I intended by it informing' he is not believed judicially. And what is meant by the ba'in that does not follow the ba'in is the kinayah that conveys irrevocable divorce by any word because it is not apparent in composition in divorce as clarified in Fath al-Qadir. Hence he said in al-Khulasa: If he said to her after the separation 'I have divorced you' and intended by it divorce, nothing occurs. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: If he divorces the mab'anah during the iddah, if it is by explicit divorce it occurs, and nothing occurs by kinayat of divorce even if he intends. His intent is except the revocable ones. But there is a difficulty from the sixth category of khul' in lieu: If he divorces her for a consideration then divorces her during the iddah, it is not valid, for this is a ba'in that followed explicitly, even though it is ba'in as we presented. So the consequence of what we presented is the validity of the khul' and there is no escape except by the intended meaning being that by its invalidity is meant the non-obligation of the consideration. And the evidence for it is that the author of al-Khulasa reversed it, and it is if he divorces her for a consideration after the khul' that it occurs and the consideration is not obligatory, and there is no difference between them as is not hidden. Then know that even if the consideration is not obligatory, acceptance by her is necessary for occurrence, as in al-Bazzaziyya: He said to her after khul' 'You are divorced on a thousand' it does not occur without her acceptance even if the consideration is not binding on her. And this is the issue of al-Jami' and it is a narration in Waqi'at al-Fatawa: He performed khul' twice then said in the iddah of the second 'I have one divorce left; I bought it from you with ten dinars to complete three,' and the husband said 'I sold the third divorce to you for ten' during the iddah, it is not valid. He explicitly stated the sixth: And if he divorces her for a consideration or performs khul' after the revocable divorce, it is valid; and if he divorces her for a consideration then performs khul' during the iddah, see how he distinguished between the revocable and the explicit ba'in, making the khul' occur after the revocable and not occurring after the explicit ba'in, which is divorce for a consideration. His statement: '(and there is no escape except by the intended being such)' this is far-fetched as in al-Nahr: And I say: I have known the escape by interpreting the explicit in their statement 'The ba'in follows the explicit, not the ba'in' as the revocable explicit, and divorce for a consideration is an explicit ba'in, so khul' does not follow it. And his statement 'and the evidence for it' is not apparent, for the difference is clearer than being hidden. For the non-obligation of consideration in the reverse, which is if he divorces her for a consideration after khul', its reason will be mentioned shortly, which is that giving the consideration is to obtain immediate deliverance, and it is already obtained, i.e. because immediate deliverance which does not depend on the passing of iddah is obtained by khul'. So if he divorces her after it, it occurs as ba'in even if it were revocable due to the separation having occurred before. And if it is for consideration, the consideration is also not obligatory for that reason. But in our issue, if he divorces her first for a consideration, the consideration is obligatory without doubt, because otherwise immediate deliverance would not be obtained, so the consideration is obligatory for obtaining the intended object; then if he performs khul' after it, it does not occur to avoid obtaining what has already been obtained, i.e. immediate deliverance. So how can the claim of non-obligation of the consideration be valid, which was obtained by the intended compensation through something supervening upon it? Rather, that supervening thing is cancelled, as it is more deserving of cancellation because the intended object was obtained before. And this aspect is also supportive of what we said that the intended by 'explicit' here includes the ba'in explicit, since there is no benefit in the occurrence of the ba'in after it, even if the first was in explicit wording. So grasp the verification of this position. 'Occurs'. H. Page 535. The Book of Divorce. Chapter on Kinayat in Divorce. The third, and the consideration is not obligatory because it is giving consideration to obtain immediate deliverance, and it is already obtained. As for the condition of her acceptance in the first issue, it is because his statement 'You are divorced on a thousand' suspends her divorce upon acceptance, so it does not occur without the condition's existence. And his statement includes what if he said to the mab'anah 'I have made you ba'in by one divorce' that it does not occur, unlike 'You are ba'in divorced' as in al-Bazzaziyya. And al-Dhakhira distinguished between them: if we cancel 'ba'in', his statement 'divorced' remains and it occurs; if we cancel 'I have made you ba'in', his statement 'by one divorce' remains, which is not effective. And we restricted it by the possibility of its being a report about the first because if it is not possible, such as if he intended by the second ba'in the severe separation, it is said that he is believed in what he intended and three occur because that is the place of separation and severe prohibition, and it is said that he is not believed because severity is an attribute of separation, so if intention is cancelled in the basis of separation because it already exists, it is cancelled in establishing the attribute of severity. This is in al-Muhit. And the commentators confined themselves to occurrence, but with a wording 'it is befitting', so occurrence is the relied-upon. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If he said to the mab'anah 'I have made you ba'in again' it occurs because it cannot be a response, i.e. it cannot be a report about the first. And in al-Qunyah: If he said to her 'You are ba'in' then said during her iddah 'You are ba'in by another divorce' it occurs. And it is befitting that if he made her ba'in then said to her 'You are ba'in' intending a second divorce, that the second occurs by his intention because by his intention it cannot be a report, like if he said 'I have made you ba'in by another' except that it might be said that occurrence is only by a word suitable for it, which is 'another', unlike mere intention. And the author indicated by the mab'anah not being a place for the ba'in that it is not a place for zihar and li'an: as for zihar, its consequence is prohibition, and prohibition is already obtained by separation; as for li'an, it is a ruling legislated for slandering wives, and the marital relationship is severed. So in al-Muhit. And if he performed ila' from her, his ila' is not valid in the ruling of the oath because in the ruling of the oath it is a suspension of separation legally, and existence of ownership is a condition for the validity of separation, whether immediate or suspended, as in real suspension. And if he gave her choice during the iddah, it is not valid, such as if he said to her 'choose' and she chose herself during the iddah, nothing occurs because it is a giving of ownership, and giving ownership without ownership is inconceivable. So in al-Bada'i'. And it cannot be said that it is suspended upon her choice so it should follow, because if the ba'in is suspended it follows. For we say it is not suspended; rather, she stands in his place, so her effectuation is an initial effectuation; there is no effect of a prior suspension. His statement: '(except if it is suspended)' means that the ba'in follows the ba'in if it is suspended before the immediate ba'in. So it is from Fayd al-Fattah al-'Alim. His statement: '(and it is befitting that if he made her ba'in etc.)' It is not hidden that its refutation is found from what passed in al-Muhit of cancellation of intention in the basis of separation because it already exists, and likewise what he presented from al-Hawi of his statement 'And nothing occurs by kinayat of divorce even if he intends' upon that their expression 'possibility of being a report' is apparent in being a caution against that which cannot be made a report except when he intends by it a second divorce, because every ba'in necessarily requires intention. So if he intends by the second ba'in divorce and it is possible to make it a report about the first, it does not occur, and the intended is not that he intends the first divorce specifically; otherwise they would have said 'if he intends by it the first'. So their turning away from this expression to the expression of the mentioned possibility is clear evidence that whenever it is possible to make the second a report, it does not occur even if he intends by it another divorce.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the matn statement 'لا البائن' (not the ba'in). The commentator explains the rule that if a man says something that constitutes a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce to a woman who is already ba'in (mab'anah), it does not take effect as a new divorce if the utterance can be interpreted as a report (khabar) about the previous ba'in. The reason is that since the woman is already irrevocably divorced, the utterance is truthful if taken as a report. Therefore, it is not treated as an initiation (insha') of a new divorce. However, this applies only to kinayat (allusive words), not to explicit words like 'taliq' because explicit words are legally determined for initiation. The commentator then discusses various applications and exceptions: (1) If a man says to an already divorced woman 'I have divorced you' (khala'tuk) intending divorce, it does not occur because it can be a report. (2) For a mab'anah in iddah, explicit divorce takes effect, but kinayat do not, even with intention. (3) A difficulty arises regarding khul' after divorce for consideration: if a man divorces his wife for a consideration (making her ba'in) then performs khul' during iddah, the khul' is not valid. The commentator resolves this by distinguishing between revocable (raj'i) and explicit ba'in divorce: the rule that ba'in does not follow ba'in applies only to kinayat, not to explicit ba'in. He clarifies that the non-obligation of consideration in certain scenarios is due to the concept of 'immediate deliverance' (khalas munajaz). The passage then addresses more details: the difference between saying 'abantuki bi-tatliqah' (I made you ba'in by one divorce) and 'anti taliq ba'in' (you are ba'in divorced), the role of intention in severing the possibility of being a report, and the application to other areas like zihar, li'an, ila', and takhyir (giving choice). Finally, the commentator mentions the exception 'except if it is suspended' (illa idha kana mu'allaqan), meaning that a suspended ba'in (e.g., 'if you enter the house, you are ba'in') does take effect even on a mab'anah because the suspension is prior to the immediate ba'in. The overall teaching is that the possibility of interpretation as a report is key, and intention alone cannot override that possibility.

Key Terms
البائن (al-bā'in): An irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) that severs the marital tie immediately and allows remarriage only with a new contract after the iddah. In this passage, it refers specifically to the utterance that conveys such a divorce.
المبانة (al-mabānah): A woman who is already irrevocably divorced (ba'in). She is the object of the second ba'in utterance.
خبراً (khabaran): A report or statement of information, as opposed to insha' (initiation). In this context, the utterance is interpreted as reporting the existing seperation rather than creating a new divorce.
منجز (munajaz): Immediate or unconditional, as opposed to mu'allaq (suspended). The text uses it in the phrase 'al-khalas al-munajaz' (immediate deliverance) and refers to an immediate ba'in divorce.
محل (mahall): The locus or subject; in this context, the mab'anah is said not to be a mahall (place) for the ba'in, meaning that she is not a valid subject for a new ba'in divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says to his mab'anah during iddah: 'I have made you ba'in again' (abantuki ukhra). According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling?
A) It does not occur because it can be a report of the first divorce.
B) It occurs because 'again' makes it incapable of being a report.
C) It occurs only if he intends a second divorce.
D) It does not occur because the word 'ba'in' is used.

Key Takeaway
A ba'in utterance to an already ba'in woman only takes effect if it cannot be interpreted as a report; intention alone does not override the possibility of being a report.

Ruling on 'Abantuk bi-Tatliqah' for a Mubannah Woman
States a ruling on a specific divorce kinayah for a mubannah woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband says 'abantuk bi-tatliqah' to a mubannah wife and distinguish it from the ruling when he says 'anti taliq ba'in'.

Core Idea
The word 'abantuk' describes an existing state and cannot effect a new divorce.

This passage addresses a subtle distinction in the use of kinayah words for divorce. For a woman already irrevocably divorced (mubannah), not every expression of separation is legally effective. The author contrasts two phrases to illustrate the principle: 'abantuk bi-tatliqah' does not effect divorce, while 'anti taliq ba'in' does.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phrases
The passage compares 'abantuk bi-tatliqah' (I have separated you with one divorce) and 'anti taliq ba'in' (you are free and separated).
2
Understand the woman's status
The woman is mubannah: she has already been divorced with an irrevocable (ba'in) divorce.
A mubannah is no longer a wife for certain kinayah pronouncements.
3
Note the ruling
For 'abantuk bi-tatliqah', no divorce occurs. For 'anti taliq ba'in', a divorce does occur.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Using the distinction from al-Dhakhirah: remove 'ba'in' → 'taliq' remains (effective); remove 'abantuk' → 'bi-tatliqah' remains (not a complete divorce pronouncement).
The word 'taliq' is itself a valid divorce term.
5
Apply the principle
For a mubannah, only words that directly effect a new divorce (like 'taliq') work; words describing an existing state (like 'abantuk') are ineffective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشمل كلامه ما لو قال للمبانة أبنتك بتطليقة فإنه لا يقع بخلاف أنت طالق بائن كما في البزازية. وفرق في الذخيرة بينهما بأن إذا ألغينا بائناً يبقى قوله «طالق» وبه يقع، ولو ألغينا أبنتك يبقى قوله بتطليقة» وهو غير مفيد.
And his speech includes the case where he said to a mubannah woman 'I have separated you with one divorce' — indeed it does not occur, unlike 'you are free and separated (taliq ba'in)' as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And a distinction was made in al-Dhakhirah between them: that if we remove 'ba'in', his statement 'taliq' remains and with it the divorce occurs; but if we remove 'abantuk', his statement 'with one divorce' remains and it is not effective.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage explains a ruling regarding the use of divorce kinayah (allusive words) for a woman already divorced with bainuna (mubannah). The word 'abantuk' (I have separated you) is not a valid divorce pronouncement for such a woman, because it describes an already existing state. In contrast, 'anti taliq ba'in' (you are free and separated) is effective because 'taliq' is a valid divorce word that can be applied even to a mubannah, as the word 'taliq' itself effects the divorce. The distinction from al-Dhakhirah illustrates that in 'anti taliq ba'in', if we remove the word 'ba'in', the word 'taliq' remains and effects divorce; but in 'abantuk bi-tatliqah', if we remove 'abantuk', only 'bi-tatliqah' (with one divorce) remains, which is not a complete sentence and thus ineffective.

Key Terms
مبانة (mubannah): A woman who has already been divorced with a bain (irrevocable) divorce.
كناية (kinayah): An allusive word that can imply divorce depending on intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One revocable divorce occurs.
B) One irrevocable divorce occurs.
C) No divorce occurs.
D) Three divorces occur if intended.

Key Takeaway
The word 'abantuk' does not effect divorce for a mubannah because it describes an existing state; only direct divorce words like 'taliq' work.

Suspended Divorce After Immediate Divorce: Hanafi vs. Zufar
Ruling and intra-madhhab dispute on suspended divorce after immediate divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a suspended divorce that occurs during iddah after an immediate divorce and explain why Zufar's objection is rejected.

Core Idea
A suspended divorce remains effective during iddah because the marriage is not fully severed until the waiting period ends.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: if a husband suspends divorce on a condition, then immediately divorces his wife, and the condition occurs during her iddah, does a second divorce take effect? Abu Hanifa and the majority say yes; Imam Zufar disagrees. The text defends the majority view through careful distinction from takhyir and zihar, showing that the suspension was made while she was a wife and that iddah preserves some marital effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband says 'If you enter the house, you are bain' (suspended, mu'allaq), then immediately says 'you are bain' (munjaz). The condition (entering the house) occurs while she is in iddah.
The immediate divorce is also bain (irrevocable).
2
State the Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, a second bain divorce occurs upon fulfillment of the condition.
The text says 'atnaa' (according to us).
3
Understand Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that after the immediate divorce, she is no longer a wife, so the suspension cannot take effect. He uses analogies to takhyir (choice) and zihar – where post-divorce conditions are ineffective by consensus.
Zufar was a prominent Hanafi imam; his view is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the suspension is a description of the divorce, not the woman. During iddah, the marriage is not completely severed – she remains a 'place' for divorce. The suspended divorce is like an immediate pronouncement upon condition occurrence.
Key distinction: the word 'bain' qualifies the divorce, not the woman's status.
5
Differentiate from takhyir and zihar
In takhyir, the husband transferred ownership of divorce to her, which he cannot do after divorce. In zihar, the prohibition (hurmah) is already established by the divorce. Suspended divorce relies on the original oath made while she was a wife, and iddah preserves enough marital connection for the condition to trigger the divorce.
The text includes detailed rebuttals from al-Dhakhirah and al-Haqa'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His statement: '(Except when it is suspended)' means that the bain [divorce] joins the bain [divorce] if it was suspended before the immediate bain divorce. It is from the bounty of al-Fattah al-'Alim. His statement: '(And it is appropriate that when he divorced her...)' It is not hidden that it is repelled by what preceded from al-Muhit of nullifying the intention in the essence of bainuna because it is already present, and likewise what he presented from al-Hawi of his statement 'Nothing occurs by the kinayat of divorce even if he intends, because their expression by 'possibility of it being news' is apparently a precaution against what cannot be made news except when he intends a second divorce, because every bain divorce necessarily requires intention. So if he intends divorce by the second 'bain' and it is possible to make it news about the first, it does not occur. And it is not meant that he intends the first divorce specifically; otherwise they would have said 'when he intends the first'. So their turning from this expression to the expression of the mentioned possibility is clear evidence that whenever it is possible to make the second news, it does not occur even if he intends another divorce. (When he said to her: 'If you enter the house, you are bain') intending divorce, then he divorced her immediately (munjazan), then the condition was found while she was in iddah – indeed another divorce occurs upon her, according to us, contrary to Zufar, because he did not mention 'you are bain' a second time to make it news; rather, what occurred is the effect of the previous suspension – which is the removal of the restriction at the occurrence of the condition – and she is a place [for divorce], so it occurs. And accordingly, it is said in al-Haqa'iq: if he said 'If you do such-and-such, then halal Allah upon me is haram', then he said 'so is the other matter', then he did one of them, a bain divorce occurs; if he did the other, another should occur, and so on – this should be memorized. And a distinction was made in al-Dhakhirah between 'you are bain' for a mubannah and the occurrence of suspended 'you are bain' after the divorce: because the suspension was valid initially since she was a place for it, we consider the suspended divorce as bain, and 'bain' becomes a description of the divorce. And the suspended [divorce] upon condition is like the immediate at the existence of the condition, so it is as if he said in iddah 'you are taliq ba'in' – if he said that, it occurs, unlike saying 'you are bain' immediately in the iddah of a mubannah, because it is a description of the woman and she is not a place, because its place is one with whom connection exists, and the connection has been severed by the divorce. And the added [to condition] is like the suspended. Even if he said to her 'you are bain tomorrow' intending divorce, then he divorced her, then tomorrow came – another divorce occurs. And if he said to her 'if you enter the house, you are bain' intending, then 'if you speak to Zaid, you are bain' intending, then she entered the house and the divorce occurred, then she spoke to Zaid – another occurs. In al-Dhakhirah, and it is an explanation of when both are suspended. We restricted it to being suspended before the immediate, because if he suspended the bain after the immediate bain divorce, the suspension is not valid, like the immediate, as we presented from al-Bada'i', and it applies to the book. And his speech includes the case where he made ila' from his wife, then divorced her before four months passed, then four months passed without him approaching her while she is in iddah – indeed it occurs according to us, contrary to Zufar. And two issues were raised against us: first, if he said 'when tomorrow comes, choose', then he divorced her, and she chose herself in iddah – nothing occurs by consensus. Second, if he suspended zihar upon a condition within the marriage, saying 'if you enter the house, you are to me like the back of my mother', then he divorced her in iddah – he does not become a muzahir by consensus. These are Zufar's arguments against us. And the answer was given regarding the first: he made her the owner of divorce tomorrow, and when he divorced her, he removed his ownership temporarily in one aspect and it remained in another, and ownership in one aspect is not sufficient for transferring ownership but is sufficient for removal, as in istilad and absolute tadbir, such that selling them is not permissible but manumitting them is permissible. Likewise this, and because what is considered in takhyir is her choice regarding the husband's strangers, while in suspension, it is the oath, not the existence of the condition; the proof is that if two witness the takhyir and another two witness the choice, then they retract, the liability is on the witnesses of choice, not takhyir; and if two witness the suspension and another two witness the existence of the condition, then they retract, the liability is on the witnesses of suspension, not the condition. And regarding the second: zihar necessitates a temporary prohibition expiated by kaffarah, and the prohibition has already been established by the divorce completely, so it cannot accept the prohibition by zihar, unlike the immediate kinayah, because it causes removal of ownership in one aspect not another before the end of the iddah, so it does not prevent the establishment of the ruling of suspension and its completion. His statement: '(For we say it is not suspended...)' has also preceded from al-Bada'i' that suspending the bain divorce during iddah is not valid, like the immediate. And his statement: '(after the divorce)' is attached to 'occurrence' not to 'suspended', as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a husband suspends divorce upon a condition before immediately divorcing his wife (with bain). The question is: if the condition occurs during the iddah, does a second divorce take effect? According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), it does, because the suspension was valid when made (since she was still a wife) and upon occurrence of the condition she is still in iddah, so the marriage is not completely severed. Zufar disagrees, arguing that after the immediate divorce she is no longer a wife, so the suspension cannot operate. The text provides a thorough answer, including two hypotheticals raised by Zufar (takhyir and zihar) and the Hanafi responses. The key distinction is that in takhyir and zihar, the rulings are based on different principles (ownership and prohibition) that are incompatible with the state of a mubannah, whereas a suspended divorce is a direct application of the original suspension. The passage also includes detailed analogies and evidentiary proofs from al-Dhakhirah, al-Haqa'iq, and al-Bada'i'.

Key Terms
معلق (mu'allaq): A divorce pronounced with a condition (suspended upon future event).
منجز (munjaz): An immediate or unconditional divorce.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period after divorce during which the woman cannot remarry and still has some legal ties to the husband.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce; the husband cannot take her back except with a new marriage and her consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a husband says 'if you enter the house, you are bain' then immediately divorces her, and she enters the house during her iddah?
A) No additional divorce occurs; only the first is valid.
B) A second bain divorce occurs.
C) The first divorce is nullified.
D) The condition is invalid because she is no longer his wife.

Key Takeaway
A suspended divorce made before an immediate divorce remains effective and triggers a second divorce if the condition occurs during iddah, because the marriage is not fully severed until the waiting period ends.

Does Tafwid Survive Ba'in Divorce and Remarriage?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tafwid after ba'in divorce and remarriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the survival of tafwid after ba'in divorce and remarriage, and evaluate which position is mufta bihi according to later Hanafi sources.

Core Idea
A husband's personal divorce does not necessarily nullify a prior delegation; divorce is multiple, so the wife's right may persist.

When a husband delegates the power of divorce to his wife by saying 'Your affair is in your hand,' and then divorces her himself with a ba'in divorce before she exercises her right, does she still have that right if he remarries her? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Understanding this dispute illuminates how the Hanafi school conceptualizes the nature of delegation (tafwid) and the multiplicity of divorce (ta'addud al-talaq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The husband says 'Your affair is in your hand whenever you wish,' then divorces her once, a ba'in divorce. He later remarries her. After the new marriage, she says 'I choose myself.' Determine whether this choice counts as a divorce.
2
State the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa says she divorces (the choice is effective). Abu Yusuf says no divorce occurs because the husband already did the delegated act.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; Muhammad is not mentioned here.
3
Analyze Each Proof
Abu Hanifa: The delegation was valid and her right attached; removal of ownership (zawal al-milk) does not nullify it because divorce is multiple, so the husband's one divorce may not be the specific act delegated. Analogy: an agent for selling a heap of grain is not removed if the principal himself sells a qafiz. Abu Yusuf: The husband executed the very act he delegated, thus removing the matter from her hand (ikhraj al-amr min yadiha).
Note the key difference: Abu Hanifa sees the delegation as a general right; Abu Yusuf sees it as specific to the husband's own act.
4
Evaluate the Tarjih
Later sources (al-Qunya, al-Bazzaziyya) indicate that after remarriage, she does not retain the power in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). The mufta bihi is non-occurrence after remarriage, but during 'iddah she retains it.
This shows how the school's later authorities resolved the disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا لو قال لها اختاري ناوياً ثم أبانها بطل التخيير حتى لو قالت بعدها اخترت نفسي لم يقع . كذا في الذخيرة والظهيرية. ثم قال في الظهيرية وفي الأمالي قال لها أمرك بيدك إذا شئت ثم طلقها واحدة بائنة ثم تزوجها فاختارت نفسها طلقت عند أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف : لا تطلق لأن الزوج فعل بنفسه ما فوض إليها فيكون إخراجاً للأمر من يدها. وجه قول أبي حنيفة أن التفويض قد صح وتعلق حقها به فلا يبطل بزوال الملك، وما قاله أبو يوسف ضعيف لأن الطلاق متعدد فلا يتعين ما أوقعه الزوج لما فوض إليها كما لو قال لغيره وهذا لا يخالف ما نقلناه هذه الصبرة ثم باع بنفسه قفيزاً لا ينعزل الوكيل ا هـ. عن البدائع لأن ما في البدائع محمول على ما إذا لم يتزوجها فلا يقع في العدة، وما في الظهيرية صريح في أنه تزوجها، وفي البزازية من الأمر باليد جعل أمرها بيدها في طلاق إن فعل كذا متى شاءت ثم خلعها على مال ثم وجد الشرط وهي في العدة، تملك الإيقاع. وإن مضت ثم تزوجها ووجد الشرط ذكر في الزيادات ما يؤخذ منه جوابه وهو عدم الوقوع وفي القنية : لا يبقى الأمر في يدها في ظاهر الرواية.
And similarly, if he said to her 'Choose' intending [divorce], then he separated her (with a ba'in divorce), the choice is void, such that if she later says 'I choose myself,' it does not occur. Thus in al-Dhakhira and al-Zahiri. Then he said in al-Zahiri and al-Amali: He said to her 'Your affair is in your hand, whenever you wish,' then he divorced her with one ba'in divorce, then he married her again, and she chose herself—it occurs as divorce according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: It does not occur because the husband himself did what he had delegated to her, thus removing the matter from her hand. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that the delegation was valid and her right became attached to it, so it is not nullified by the removal of ownership; and what Abu Yusuf said is weak because divorce is multiple, so it is not determined that what the husband did is the same as what was delegated to her, just as if he said to someone else [and he acted], and this does not contradict what we narrated: 'This heap, then he himself sold a qafiz, the agent is not removed.' From al-Bada'i, because what is in al-Bada'i is understood as when he did not marry her, so it does not occur in the 'iddah, and what is in al-Zahiri is explicit that he married her. And in al-Bazzaziyya from 'amr al-yad: He made her affair in her hand for divorce if she does such-and-such whenever she wishes, then he divorced her by khul' for money, then the condition occurred while she was in 'iddah—she has the power to effect [divorce]. But if her 'iddah passed, then he married her again and the condition occurred, it is mentioned in al-Ziyadat what is taken from it as a response, which is non-occurrence, and in al-Qunya: The affair does not remain in her hand in the apparent narration.
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the continuation of a delegation of divorce (tafwid) after the husband has already divorced his wife with a ba'in divorce and then remarried her. The issue arises when a husband tells his wife 'Your affair is in your hand' (amruki bi-yadiki) or 'Choose' (ikhtari). If he then divorces her with a single ba'in divorce before she chooses, and later remarries her, does she still have the right to divorce herself by choosing? Abu Hanifa holds that she does, because the delegation was valid and her right is established; it is not voided by the removal of marital ownership since divorce is multiple—the husband's own divorce does not necessarily consume the delegated power. He gives an analogy: if a person appoints an agent to sell a heap of grain, and then the principal himself sells a qafiz, the agent is not removed; similarly here. Abu Yusuf argues that the husband's own act of divorcing removes the matter from her hands because he exercised the very power he gave her. The text then notes that the case is different if the husband did not remarry her—then the delegation does not revive. Later sources like al-Bazzaziyya add a condition: if after khul' the condition occurs during 'iddah, she retains the power; but if she leaves 'iddah and he remarries her, she does not. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that she does not retain the power after remarriage, as stated in al-Qunya.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwid): Delegation of the power to divorce to the wife, e.g., by saying 'Your affair is in your hand.'
بائن (ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately and requires a new marriage for re-cohabitation.
تخيير (takhyir): Giving the wife a choice regarding divorce, often by saying 'Choose yourself' (ikhtari).
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (later Hanafi sources), what is the ruling if a husband, after saying 'Your affair is in your hand,' divorces his wife with a ba'in divorce, and then after her 'iddah, remarries her, and she says 'I choose myself'?
A) The divorce occurs, and she becomes unlawful to him.
B) The divorce does not occur; she remains married.
C) The divorce occurs only if she had already chosen during the first marriage.
D) The divorce is suspended until the husband confirms it.

Key Takeaway
An intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether a wife's delegated divorce right survives her husband's own divorce and subsequent remarriage; the relied-upon position is that it does not survive remarriage, but it does survive during 'iddah.

The Rule of Attachment: Divorce in 'Idda Requires Prior Revocable Divorce
Ruling with proof on the condition for effective divorce in 'idda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a divorce pronounced during the 'idda is only effective if the prior separation was a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) and identify scenarios where it is ineffective.

Core Idea
Divorce in 'idda only attaches if the prior separation was itself a revocable divorce.

This passage explains a key limitation: not every divorce uttered during the waiting period takes effect. The rule is that a subsequent divorce only attaches ('lahaqa') to a prior divorce that was revocable. If the prior separation was a final divorce (bā’in) or a judicial annulment (faskh), the later divorce does not count. This distinction is crucial for determining the number of divorces a husband has issued and the possibility of reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The husband pronounces a divorce (talaq) during the wife's 'idda. Determine the nature of the prior separation that began the 'idda.
2
Apply the core rule
The subsequent divorce takes effect only if the prior separation was a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i). If it was a final divorce (talaq bā’in) or a non-divorce separation (faskh), the subsequent divorce does not occur.
The passage states: 'لا بائن لمثله ما علقا' (not a final, like it, whatever was suspended).
3
Recognize exceptions
The rule applies to all separations that are not revocable divorces, including those caused by option of puberty, emancipation, apostasy, judicial annulment, etc.
The text mentions 'كل فرقة توجب الحرمة المؤبدة لا يلحقها الطلاق' (every separation that necessitates permanent prohibition, divorce does not attach to it).
4
Distinguish between revocable and irrevocable
Ensure you can differentiate between talaq raj'i (revocable) and talaq bā’in (irrevocable) as only the former allows further divorces in the 'idda.
The term 'bā’in' here refers to a final divorce that ends the marriage immediately, not a revocable one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ا هـ. قال شارح المنظومة عبد البر رحمه الله قلت : وقد فات الشيخين التنبيه على أن ذلك خاص بالعدة وإن كان ذلك من المعلوم من خارج لأن تمام معنى الضابط متوقف عليه فقلت منبهاً على ذلك بيتاً مفرداً من الرجز : بعدة كل طلاق لحقا لا بائن لمثله ما علقا ثم قولي الحقا» مشعر بكون اللاحق هو المعلق ووصفنا البائن بأنه مثل البائن مشعر بإخراج البينونة الكبرى لما فيها من الخلاف الذي قدمته ا هـ . وقيد المؤلف بكون السابق طلاقاً لأنه لو كان فرقة بغير طلاق كالفرقة بخيار البلوغ أو العتاقة بعد الدخول فإنه لا يقع الطلاق في عدته، وكل فرقة توجب الحرمة المؤبدة لا يلحقها الطلاق، وإذا أسلم أحد الزوجين لا يقع على الآخر طلاقه كذا في البزازية. وإذا ارتد ولحق بدار الحرب فطلقها في العدة لم يقع لانقطاع العصمة، فإن عاد إلى دار الإسلام وهي في العدة وقع، وإذا ارتدت ولحقت لم يقع عليها طلاقه، فإن عادت قبل الحيض لم يقع كذلك عند أبي حنيفة لبطلان العدة باللحاق ثم لا تعود بخلاف المرتد كذا في البدائع. وفي الذخيرة والحاصل أن كل فرقة هي فسخ من صريح طلاق المرء يلحق مثله ويلحق أيضاً بائناً كان قبله كذا عكسه لا بائن بعد بائن سوى بائن قد كان علق فعله

قوله : (وإذا أسلم أحد الزوجين الخ) قال الرملي : هذا في طلاق أهل الحرب وقد أتبعه في الخلاصة بعد ذكر ما ذكره البزازي هنا بقوله في باب طلاق أهل الحرب من الأصل ولا يخفى ما في ذكره هنا مطلقاً من الخفاء. قال العقيلي في المنهاج : حربية خرجت مسلمة ثم خرج زوجها بأمان فطلقها لا يقع فإن أسلم الزوج أو صار ذمياً ثم طلق يقع عند محمد رحمه الله وهو قول أبي يوسف الأول، وفي قوله الآخر لا يقع .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : وفي المنتقى عن أبي يوسف ما يدل على أنه لا عدة على المهاجرة : إذا خرج الحربي مسلماً وتركها في دار الحرب فلا عدة عليها في قولهم جميعاً فاعلم ذلك اهـ . قلت : وقدم المؤلف في أول كتاب الطلاق عن الفتح أنه لا يقع الطلاق في عدة عن فسخ إلا في تفريق القاضي بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام وفي ارتداد أحدهما مطلقاً اهـ. لكن فيه أنه إذا كانت الآبية فإن هذه الفرقة فسخ كان الآبي هو الزوج وهو من أهل الطلاق فهي طلاق . قوله : (وفي الذخيرة الخ ذكر في الذخيرة بعد ذلك بيان الفرقة التي هي طلاق والتي ليست بطلاق فقال : الفرقة بالجب والعنة طلاق بلا خلاف إذا كان الزوج من أهل الطلاق وإلا بأن كان صبياً فقيل فرقة بغير طلاق، وقيل بطلاق ويكون بائناً ويكون المهر كاملاً وعليها العدة. ولا تقع الفرقة إلا بقضاء القاضي والفرقة بخيار البلوغ وهي فسخ ولا تقع إلا بالقضاء، وكذا الفرقة بعدم الكفاءة والتقصير في المهر هي فسخ لا طلاق والفرقة بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام بتفريق القاضي تكون طلاقاً إن كان الآبي هو الزوج وكان من أهل الطلاق وإلا بأن كان صبياً عقل الإسلام وأبي فقيل طلاق عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقيل هي فرقة بغير طلاق إجماعاً وإن كانت الآبية بأن أسلم هو وهي مجوسية أبت أن تسلم فهي فرقة بغير طلاق إجماعاً ولا تقع إلا بالقضاء أيضاً والفرقة باللعان طلاق ولا تقع إلا بالقضاء . وكل وجه لا يقع الطلاق في عدتها، وكل فرقة هي طلاق يقع الطلاق فيها في العدة ا هـ . وقدمنا شيئاً منه في أول كتاب الطلاق والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب
End. The commentator of the Manzuma, Abd al-Barr, may Allah have mercy on him, said: I said: And the two shaykhs missed pointing out that this is specific to the 'idda, even though that is known from outside, because the complete meaning of the rule depends on it. So I said, alerting to that, a single line of rajaz: 'In the 'idda of every divorce, it attaches, not a final separation, like it, whatever was suspended.' Then my saying 'attaches' indicates that what attaches is the suspended one, and our description of the final separation as 'like the final' indicates the exclusion of the major final separation because of the disagreement about it that I presented. And the author restricted it to the prior being a divorce, because if it were a separation without divorce, like separation by the option of puberty or emancipation after consummation, then divorce in its 'idda does not occur. And every separation that necessitates permanent prohibition, divorce does not attach to it. And if one of the spouses becomes Muslim, the other's divorce does not occur upon him. Thus in al-Bazaziyya. And if he apostatizes and joins the abode of war and divorces her in the 'idda, it does not occur due to the severance of the marital bond. If he returns to the abode of Islam while she is in the 'idda, it occurs. And if she apostatizes and joins, her divorce does not occur upon her. If she returns before menstruation, it also does not occur according to Abu Hanifa because the 'idda is invalidated by the joining and then does not return, contrary to the apostate. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Dhakhira: And the summary is that every separation that is a faskh from explicit divorce of a man attaches to its like and also attaches to a final separation that was before it, likewise its opposite, not a final after a final except a final that was suspended. Statement: (And if one of the spouses becomes Muslim, etc.) al-Ramli said: This is about the divorce of the people of war. And he followed it in al-Khulasa after mentioning what al-Bazazi mentioned here with his saying in the chapter on divorce of the people of war from the original, and it is not hidden that there is obscurity in mentioning it here absolutely. al-Uqayli said in al-Minhaj: A free woman who left as a Muslim then her husband came out under safe conduct and divorced her, it does not occur. If the husband becomes Muslim or becomes a dhimmi and then divorces, it occurs according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, and it is the first statement of Abu Yusuf, and in his other statement it does not occur. And in al-Tatar Khaniyya: And in al-Muntaqa from Abu Yusuf is an indication that there is no 'idda upon the emigrant woman: if the combatant comes out Muslim and leaves her in the abode of war, then there is no 'idda upon her in their collective opinion. So know that. I said: And the author stated earlier in the beginning of the book of divorce, from al-Fath, that divorce does not occur in the 'idda of a faskh except in the case of the judge's separation due to one of them refusing Islam and in the apostasy of one of them absolutely. But in it, if the one refusing is the husband, then this separation is a faskh, if the one refusing is the husband and he is capable of divorce, then it is a divorce. Statement: (And in al-Dhakhira, etc.) He mentioned in al-Dhakhira after that an explanation of the separation that is a divorce and that which is not a divorce. He said: Separation by impotence and defect is a divorce without dispute if the husband is capable of divorce; otherwise if he was a child, it is said it is a separation without divorce, and it is said it is a divorce and it is final and the mahr is complete and the 'idda is upon her. The separation does not occur except by the judge's ruling. Separation by the option of puberty is a faskh and does not occur except by the judge's ruling. Likewise, separation due to lack of competence and deficiency in the mahr is a faskh, not a divorce. Separation by one of them refusing Islam by the judge's ruling is a divorce if the one refusing is the husband and is capable of divorce; otherwise if he was a child who understood Islam and refused, it is said it is a divorce according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and it is said it is a separation without divorce by consensus. And if the one refusing is the woman, if he became Muslim and she is a Magian who refuses to become Muslim, it is a separation without divorce by consensus, and it does not occur except by the judge's ruling as well. Separation by li'an is a divorce and does not occur except by the judge's ruling. And every case where divorce does not occur in its 'idda, and every separation that is a divorce, divorce occurs in it in the 'idda. End. And we have presented something of it earlier in the beginning of the book of divorce. And Allah, the Exalted, knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and the refuge.
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the conditions under which a husband's divorce uttered during the wife's 'idda is effective. The author of al-Hidayah (or the sharh) clarifies that the rule 'divorce attaches to its like' applies only when the prior separation was itself a revocable divorce. If the prior separation was a faskh (judicial annulment) or a final divorce (bainuna), then a subsequent divorce during the 'idda does not take effect. The text enumerates several types of separation: option of puberty, emancipation, apostasy, emigration, impotence, lack of competence, refusal of Islam, and li'an. For each, it states whether it counts as a divorce or a faskh, and whether divorce in the 'idda applies. The author cites authorities like al-Bazaziyya, al-Bada'i', al-Dhakhira, and mentions intra-Hanafi differences (Abu Yusuf's two opinions, Muhammad's view, Abu Hanifa's view). The ruling also covers the effect of apostasy and joining the abode of war on both the 'idda and the effectiveness of divorce. The passage concludes with the general principle: every separation that is a divorce allows subsequent divorce in its 'idda; every other separation does not. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi family law regarding the timing of divorce.

Key Terms
العدة (al-‘idda): The waiting period a woman must observe after separation from her husband before she can remarry.
الفرقة (al-furqa): Separation between spouses, which can be either a divorce (talaq) or a judicial annulment (faskh).
البائن (al-bā’in): A final divorce that ends the marriage irrevocably without the possibility of revocability during the 'idda.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband divorces his wife during her 'idda after a judicial annulment (faskh) due to her option of puberty, does the divorce take effect?
A) Yes, because it is still a divorce.
B) No, because divorce in 'idda only applies after a revocable divorce, not after a faskh.
C) Yes, but only if she had not yet remarried.
D) No, unless the husband intended it as a final divorce.

Key Takeaway
A divorce during 'idda is effective only if the prior separation was a revocable divorce; all other separations (faskh, final divorce) prevent attachment.

Talaq — Divorce
