10 min
Distinguishing Talaq from Faskh in Separation Cases
Listing and classifying separation types as talaq or faskh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify each type of marital separation (impotence, option of puberty, incompatibility, refusal of Islam, li'an) as either a revocable divorce (talaq) or a judicial annulment (faskh) according to the Hanafi school, and identify which allow subsequent divorce in the 'idda.

Core Idea
Only separations that are revocable divorces allow further divorces in the 'idda; all others do not.

The author of al-Dhakhira provides a comprehensive list of separation scenarios and categorizes each as talaq or faskh. This classification determines whether a later divorce during the 'idda takes effect. Understanding these categories is essential for family law practice, as it affects the number of divorces a husband has and the possibility of remarriage.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of separation cases
The passage lists: impotence/defect (jabb/'inna), option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh), lack of competence (adam al-kafa'a), deficiency in mahr, refusal of Islam (iba' 'an al-Islam) by husband or wife, and li'an (mutual imprecation).
2
Determine for each case whether it is talaq or faskh
Impotence: talaq if husband is capable of divorce, otherwise dispute. Option of puberty: faskh. Lack of competence: faskh. Refusal of Islam by husband: talaq if he is capable. Refusal by wife: faskh. Li'an: talaq.
Note the conditions: the husband must be capable of divorce (baligh, sane) for talaq to occur.
3
Apply the secondary rule
If the separation is talaq, a subsequent divorce in the 'idda attaches. If faskh, it does not.
4
Identify intra-Hanafi differences
For the case of a child who understands Islam and refuses, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is talaq; others say faskh.
This affects whether a subsequent divorce in 'idda can occur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ا هـ. قال شارح المنظومة عبد البر رحمه الله قلت : وقد فات الشيخين التنبيه على أن ذلك خاص بالعدة وإن كان ذلك من المعلوم من خارج لأن تمام معنى الضابط متوقف عليه فقلت منبهاً على ذلك بيتاً مفرداً من الرجز : بعدة كل طلاق لحقا لا بائن لمثله ما علقا ثم قولي الحقا» مشعر بكون اللاحق هو المعلق ووصفنا البائن بأنه مثل البائن مشعر بإخراج البينونة الكبرى لما فيها من الخلاف الذي قدمته ا هـ . وقيد المؤلف بكون السابق طلاقاً لأنه لو كان فرقة بغير طلاق كالفرقة بخيار البلوغ أو العتاقة بعد الدخول فإنه لا يقع الطلاق في عدته، وكل فرقة توجب الحرمة المؤبدة لا يلحقها الطلاق، وإذا أسلم أحد الزوجين لا يقع على الآخر طلاقه كذا في البزازية. وإذا ارتد ولحق بدار الحرب فطلقها في العدة لم يقع لانقطاع العصمة، فإن عاد إلى دار الإسلام وهي في العدة وقع، وإذا ارتدت ولحقت لم يقع عليها طلاقه، فإن عادت قبل الحيض لم يقع كذلك عند أبي حنيفة لبطلان العدة باللحاق ثم لا تعود بخلاف المرتد كذا في البدائع. وفي الذخيرة والحاصل أن كل فرقة هي فسخ من صريح طلاق المرء يلحق مثله ويلحق أيضاً بائناً كان قبله كذا عكسه لا بائن بعد بائن سوى بائن قد كان علق فعله

قوله : (وإذا أسلم أحد الزوجين الخ) قال الرملي : هذا في طلاق أهل الحرب وقد أتبعه في الخلاصة بعد ذكر ما ذكره البزازي هنا بقوله في باب طلاق أهل الحرب من الأصل ولا يخفى ما في ذكره هنا مطلقاً من الخفاء. قال العقيلي في المنهاج : حربية خرجت مسلمة ثم خرج زوجها بأمان فطلقها لا يقع فإن أسلم الزوج أو صار ذمياً ثم طلق يقع عند محمد رحمه الله وهو قول أبي يوسف الأول، وفي قوله الآخر لا يقع .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : وفي المنتقى عن أبي يوسف ما يدل على أنه لا عدة على المهاجرة : إذا خرج الحربي مسلماً وتركها في دار الحرب فلا عدة عليها في قولهم جميعاً فاعلم ذلك اهـ . قلت : وقدم المؤلف في أول كتاب الطلاق عن الفتح أنه لا يقع الطلاق في عدة عن فسخ إلا في تفريق القاضي بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام وفي ارتداد أحدهما مطلقاً اهـ. لكن فيه أنه إذا كانت الآبية فإن هذه الفرقة فسخ كان الآبي هو الزوج وهو من أهل الطلاق فهي طلاق . قوله : (وفي الذخيرة الخ ذكر في الذخيرة بعد ذلك بيان الفرقة التي هي طلاق والتي ليست بطلاق فقال : الفرقة بالجب والعنة طلاق بلا خلاف إذا كان الزوج من أهل الطلاق وإلا بأن كان صبياً فقيل فرقة بغير طلاق، وقيل بطلاق ويكون بائناً ويكون المهر كاملاً وعليها العدة. ولا تقع الفرقة إلا بقضاء القاضي والفرقة بخيار البلوغ وهي فسخ ولا تقع إلا بالقضاء، وكذا الفرقة بعدم الكفاءة والتقصير في المهر هي فسخ لا طلاق والفرقة بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام بتفريق القاضي تكون طلاقاً إن كان الآبي هو الزوج وكان من أهل الطلاق وإلا بأن كان صبياً عقل الإسلام وأبي فقيل طلاق عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقيل هي فرقة بغير طلاق إجماعاً وإن كانت الآبية بأن أسلم هو وهي مجوسية أبت أن تسلم فهي فرقة بغير طلاق إجماعاً ولا تقع إلا بالقضاء أيضاً والفرقة باللعان طلاق ولا تقع إلا بالقضاء . وكل وجه لا يقع الطلاق في عدتها، وكل فرقة هي طلاق يقع الطلاق فيها في العدة ا هـ . وقدمنا شيئاً منه في أول كتاب الطلاق والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب
End. The commentator of the Manzuma, Abd al-Barr, may Allah have mercy on him, said: I said: And the two shaykhs missed pointing out that this is specific to the 'idda, even though that is known from outside, because the complete meaning of the rule depends on it. So I said, alerting to that, a single line of rajaz: 'In the 'idda of every divorce, it attaches, not a final separation, like it, whatever was suspended.' Then my saying 'attaches' indicates that what attaches is the suspended one, and our description of the final separation as 'like the final' indicates the exclusion of the major final separation because of the disagreement about it that I presented. And the author restricted it to the prior being a divorce, because if it were a separation without divorce, like separation by the option of puberty or emancipation after consummation, then divorce in its 'idda does not occur. And every separation that necessitates permanent prohibition, divorce does not attach to it. And if one of the spouses becomes Muslim, the other's divorce does not occur upon him. Thus in al-Bazaziyya. And if he apostatizes and joins the abode of war and divorces her in the 'idda, it does not occur due to the severance of the marital bond. If he returns to the abode of Islam while she is in the 'idda, it occurs. And if she apostatizes and joins, her divorce does not occur upon her. If she returns before menstruation, it also does not occur according to Abu Hanifa because the 'idda is invalidated by the joining and then does not return, contrary to the apostate. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Dhakhira: And the summary is that every separation that is a faskh from explicit divorce of a man attaches to its like and also attaches to a final separation that was before it, likewise its opposite, not a final after a final except a final that was suspended. Statement: (And if one of the spouses becomes Muslim, etc.) al-Ramli said: This is about the divorce of the people of war. And he followed it in al-Khulasa after mentioning what al-Bazazi mentioned here with his saying in the chapter on divorce of the people of war from the original, and it is not hidden that there is obscurity in mentioning it here absolutely. al-Uqayli said in al-Minhaj: A free woman who left as a Muslim then her husband came out under safe conduct and divorced her, it does not occur. If the husband becomes Muslim or becomes a dhimmi and then divorces, it occurs according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, and it is the first statement of Abu Yusuf, and in his other statement it does not occur. And in al-Tatar Khaniyya: And in al-Muntaqa from Abu Yusuf is an indication that there is no 'idda upon the emigrant woman: if the combatant comes out Muslim and leaves her in the abode of war, then there is no 'idda upon her in their collective opinion. So know that. I said: And the author stated earlier in the beginning of the book of divorce, from al-Fath, that divorce does not occur in the 'idda of a faskh except in the case of the judge's separation due to one of them refusing Islam and in the apostasy of one of them absolutely. But in it, if the one refusing is the husband, then this separation is a faskh, if the one refusing is the husband and he is capable of divorce, then it is a divorce. Statement: (And in al-Dhakhira, etc.) He mentioned in al-Dhakhira after that an explanation of the separation that is a divorce and that which is not a divorce. He said: Separation by impotence and defect is a divorce without dispute if the husband is capable of divorce; otherwise if he was a child, it is said it is a separation without divorce, and it is said it is a divorce and it is final and the mahr is complete and the 'idda is upon her. The separation does not occur except by the judge's ruling. Separation by the option of puberty is a faskh and does not occur except by the judge's ruling. Likewise, separation due to lack of competence and deficiency in the mahr is a faskh, not a divorce. Separation by one of them refusing Islam by the judge's ruling is a divorce if the one refusing is the husband and is capable of divorce; otherwise if he was a child who understood Islam and refused, it is said it is a divorce according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and it is said it is a separation without divorce by consensus. And if the one refusing is the woman, if he became Muslim and she is a Magian who refuses to become Muslim, it is a separation without divorce by consensus, and it does not occur except by the judge's ruling as well. Separation by li'an is a divorce and does not occur except by the judge's ruling. And every case where divorce does not occur in its 'idda, and every separation that is a divorce, divorce occurs in it in the 'idda. End. And we have presented something of it earlier in the beginning of the book of divorce. And Allah, the Exalted, knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and the refuge.
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the conditions under which a husband's divorce uttered during the wife's 'idda is effective. The author of al-Hidayah (or the sharh) clarifies that the rule 'divorce attaches to its like' applies only when the prior separation was itself a revocable divorce. If the prior separation was a faskh (judicial annulment) or a final divorce (bainuna), then a subsequent divorce during the 'idda does not take effect. The text enumerates several types of separation: option of puberty, emancipation, apostasy, emigration, impotence, lack of competence, refusal of Islam, and li'an. For each, it states whether it counts as a divorce or a faskh, and whether divorce in the 'idda applies. The author cites authorities like al-Bazaziyya, al-Bada'i', al-Dhakhira, and mentions intra-Hanafi differences (Abu Yusuf's two opinions, Muhammad's view, Abu Hanifa's view). The ruling also covers the effect of apostasy and joining the abode of war on both the 'idda and the effectiveness of divorce. The passage concludes with the general principle: every separation that is a divorce allows subsequent divorce in its 'idda; every other separation does not. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi family law regarding the timing of divorce.

Key Terms
الجب والعنة (al-jabb wa al-‘inna): Impotence and defect in the husband that prevent consummation.
خيار البلوغ (khiyār al-bulūgh): The option of puberty, which allows a minor married before puberty to nullify the marriage upon reaching puberty.
اللعان (al-li‘ān): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of adultery and she denies it, resulting in separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following separations is classified as a talaq (divorce)?
A) Separation due to the wife's option of puberty.
B) Separation due to lack of compatibility (adam al-kafa'a).
C) Separation due to the husband's impotence, if he is capable of divorce.
D) Separation due to the wife's refusal to become Muslim after the husband's conversion.

Key Takeaway
Only separations classified as talaq (like impotence, li'an, and husband's refusal of Islam) allow a subsequent divorce in the 'idda; faskh separations block it.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
10 min
The Effect of Apostasy and Emigration on Divorce in 'Idda
Ruling on apostasy and emigration affecting divorce in 'idda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how apostasy and emigration to dar al-harb affect the validity of a later divorce during the 'idda, including the differences between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Apostasy severs the marriage bond, making later divorce in 'idda ineffective in many cases.

The passage addresses complex scenarios where apostasy or emigration occurs. Depending on who apostatizes and whether they return, the 'idda may be invalidated or the husband's divorce may not take effect. The Hanafi Imams have differing opinions, particularly on the wife's apostasy and the husband's return to Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
Consider cases where the husband apostatizes and joins dar al-harb, or the wife apostatizes and joins, or one spouse emigrates.
2
Determine the effect on the marriage bond
Apostasy severs the marriage immediately. Emigration may or may not affect the marriage depending on the circumstances.
3
Analyze the effect on the 'idda
If the marriage is severed, the 'idda may be invalidated or may continue if the spouse returns. Abu Hanifa holds that the wife's apostasy invalidates her 'idda permanently; the apostate husband's 'idda continues if he returns.
4
Consider the effectiveness of a divorce after return
If the husband returns to Islam during the 'idda, his divorce takes effect according to some views. If the wife returns, her divorce does not take effect according to Abu Hanifa.
Abu Yusuf has two opinions on the husband's return.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi differences
Abu Hanifa's view on wife's apostasy differs from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Also, Muhammad and Abu Yusuf's first opinion agree on the husband's return as effective.

And if the one refusing is the woman, if he became Muslim and she is a Magian who refuses to become Muslim, it is a separation without divorce by consensus, and it does not occur except by the judge's ruling as well. Separation by li'an is a divorce and does not occur except by the judge's ruling. And every case where divorce does not occur in its 'idda, and every separation that is a divorce, divorce occurs in it in the 'idda. End. And we have presented something of it earlier in the beginning of the book of divorce. And Allah, the Exalted, knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and the refuge.
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the conditions under which a husband's divorce uttered during the wife's 'idda is effective. The author of al-Hidayah (or the sharh) clarifies that the rule 'divorce attaches to its like' applies only when the prior separation was itself a revocable divorce. If the prior separation was a faskh (judicial annulment) or a final divorce (bainuna), then a subsequent divorce during the 'idda does not take effect. The text enumerates several types of separation: option of puberty, emancipation, apostasy, emigration, impotence, lack of competence, refusal of Islam, and li'an. For each, it states whether it counts as a divorce or a faskh, and whether divorce in the 'idda applies. The author cites authorities like al-Bazaziyya, al-Bada'i', al-Dhakhira, and mentions intra-Hanafi differences (Abu Yusuf's two opinions, Muhammad's view, Abu Hanifa's view). The ruling also covers the effect of apostasy and joining the abode of war on both the 'idda and the effectiveness of divorce. The passage concludes with the general principle: every separation that is a divorce allows subsequent divorce in its 'idda; every other separation does not. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi family law regarding the timing of divorce.

Key Terms
الحراب (al-harb): Abode of war; the territory not under Muslim rule where hostilities may be permitted.
المهاجرة (al-muhājira): A woman who emigrates from dar al-harb to dar al-Islam, often as a Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Her 'idda continues from where it stopped.
B) Her 'idda is invalidated and does not restart.
C) Her 'idda restarts from the day she returns.
D) Her 'idda is unaffected.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy severs the marriage bond, making a divorce ineffective until the bond is restored by return to Islam during the 'idda; the wife's apostasy has different consequences.

Delegation of Divorce: The Ruling on 'Choose' with Intention
Ruling on delegation via 'choose' with proofs and objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule when a husband says 'choose' intending divorce, and identify the proofs from consensus and Quran.

Core Idea
When a husband says 'choose' intending divorce, the wife's immediate choice effects one revocable divorce.

In this passage, the author introduces the chapter on delegation of divorce (tafwid), categorizing it into three types: delegation, agency, and message. He then focuses on the first type, specifically the wording 'choose' (ikhtari). The core ruling is that if the husband intends divorce and the wife chooses herself in the same sitting, one divorce occurs. The author provides proofs from the consensus of the Companions and a Quranic verse, and addresses several objections. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled? The husband says 'choose' to his wife intending divorce. The ruling: if she chooses herself in that sitting, one revocable divorce (ba'in) occurs.
The ruling is specific to the wording of choice (takhyir) with intention.
2
Recognize the condition of intention
The husband's intention is essential. If he did not intend divorce, the delegation is not effective even if she chooses. The text explicitly says 'intending divorce'.
This distinguishes delegation from mere joking.
3
Understand the option of assembly
The wife must choose in the same sitting (majlis) as the husband's statement. This is called 'option of the assembly'. The author argues this is proven by the consensus of the Companions.
If she delays, her right to choose lapses.
4
Examine the proofs
The author cites the silent consensus of the Companions and the Quranic verse (al-Ahzab:28) where the Prophet gave his wives a choice. He also refutes the weak hadith of Aisha that might suggest otherwise.
The consensus is considered strong evidence (qat'i) in Hanafi usul.
5
Address the objections
Objections raised: How can the wife be granted the act while the husband still owns the marriage? Answer: She is granted the power to effect the divorce, not ownership of the marriage itself. Another objection about agency is deferred to a later section.
These objections refine the understanding of delegation as empowerment (tamlik) rather than ownership transfer.

Chapter on Delegation of Divorce. When he finished explaining what the husband himself effects explicitly and by allusion, he began on what someone else effects with his permission, which are three types: delegation, agency, and message. Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on delegation of divorce (tafwid). The author first categorizes the types of divorce that someone other than the husband can effect: delegation (tafwid), agency (tawkil), and message (risala). Delegation to the wife is by specific wordings: choice (takhyir), command of the hand (amr bi al-yad), and will (mashi'a). The first ruling presented is for the word 'choose' (ikhtari). If the husband says to his wife 'choose' intending divorce, and she chooses herself (i.e., states that she chooses divorce) in the same sitting, she becomes separated by one revocable divorce. The author provides proofs: consensus of the Companions on the option of the assembly, and the Quranic verse (al-Ahzab:28) where the Prophet (PBUH) gave his wives a choice. The passage then addresses objections: How can the wife be granted the act while the husband still owns the marriage? The answer is that she is granted the power to effect the divorce, not ownership of the marriage itself. Another objection compares it to agency: if someone appoints an agent to release a debt, the agent acts for himself but can still be revoked. A similar discussion is deferred to the section on 'will'. The passage also mentions a disagreement about whether the option of the assembly is required; Ibn al-Mundhir argued against it, but the author refutes him. Towards the end, a line about a Magian woman and li'an appears, which seems out of place and is likely a scribal error. The lesson establishes the foundational rule for one form of delegation.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwīḍ): Delegation of the power to divorce from the husband to the wife.
تخيير (takhyīr): The husband giving the wife a choice, typically 'choose' (ikhtari), which can lead to divorce if she chooses herself.
مجلس (majlis): The sitting or gathering in which the husband makes the offer of choice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a husband says 'choose' intending divorce, one revocable divorce occurs if the wife chooses immediately in the same sitting, based on the Companions' consensus.

The Ruling of Saying 'Ikhtari' Intending Divorce
States ruling and proves it with ijma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband says 'ikhtari' intending divorce and explain the proof from the Companions' consensus.

Core Idea
When the husband says 'choose' intending divorce, the wife's choice in the same sitting effects one irrevocable divorce, proven by silent consensus.

This passage addresses the first type of divorce by delegation (tafwid): the husband saying 'Ikhtari' (choose) with the intention of divorce. The ruling hinges on two conditions: the husband's intention and the wife's immediate choice in the same sitting. The proof is the silent consensus (ijma sukuti) of the Companions, which is our focus here.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The husband says 'Ikhtari' intending divorce; the wife chooses in the same sitting. The ruling: she becomes divorced by one irrevocable (ba'in) divorce.
The divorce is ba'in, not raj'i, meaning the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the silent consensus of the Companions that the wife given choice has the option of the sitting (khiyar al-majlis). This is an ijmāʿ sukūtī, where some companions explicitly stated it and no known opposition was reliably transmitted.
The narration that ʿAlī (ra) opposed is not established.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The consensus establishes that the wife's choice in the sitting is legally effective. Since the consensus includes both the option of the sitting and the ensuing divorce, the ruling is derived directly.
The weak hadith about consulting parents does not apply here as it refers to a different context.
4
Note the conditions
Two conditions are required: (1) the husband must intend divorce (niyya) – without it, no delegation; (2) the wife must choose in the same sitting (khiyar al-majlis). If she leaves or starts another act, her option is lost.
Intention can be inferred in court from circumstantial evidence (dalalat al-hal) like anger or talk of divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب تفويض الطلاق

التصرف والتوكيل الإقدار على التصرف فاندفعت هذه الشبهة ا هـ . وفيه نظر لأن التمليك الإقدار الشرعي على نفس التصرف ابتداء، والتوكيل الإقدار الشرعي على نفس التصرف لا ابتداء كما أشار إليه في فتح القدير في أول كتاب البيع وهو الحق، لأنه لا معنى للإقرار على المحل إلا باعتبار التصرف فيه. وفي المعراج لا يلزم من التمليك عدم صحة الرجوع لانتقاضه بالهبة فإنها تمليك ويصح الرجوع لكنه تمليك يخالف سائر التمليكات من حيث إنه يبقى إلى ما وراء المجلس إذا كانت غائبة ولا يتوقف على القبول لكونها تطلق نفسها بعد التفويض وهو بعدم تمام التمليك قيد بالنية لأنه من الكنايات ودلالة الحال قائمة مقامها قضاء لا ديانة، والدلالة مذاكرة الطلاق أو الغضب، وقدمنا أنه مما تمحض للجواب والقول قوله مع اليمين في عدم النية أو الدلالة وتقبل بينتها على إثبات الغضب أو المذاكرة لا على النية إلا إذا قامت على إقراره بها كما ذكره الولوالجي. وإذا لم يصدق قضاء لا يسعها الإقامة معه إلا بنكاح مستقبل لأنها كالقاضي. وإنما ترك ذكر الدلالة هنا للعلم مما قدمه أول الكنايات. وأراد بنية الطلاق نية تفويضه وقيد بالمجلس لأنها لو قامت عنه أو أخذت في عمل آخر بطل خيارها كما سنذكره. وأفاد بذكر مجلسها أنه لا اعتبار بمجلسه، فلو خيرها ثم قام هو لم يبطل بخلاف قيامها كذا في البدائع. والحق ما في الذخيرة وفي جامع الفصولين أنه تمليك فيه معنى التعليق فلكونه تمليكاً
Chapter on Delegation of Divorce. When he finished explaining what the husband himself effects explicitly and allusively, he began on what someone else effects with his permission, which is three types: delegation, agency, and letter. Delegation to her is with the words of choice, command by hand, and will. He presented the first due to its being established by explicit proof: his statement: (And if he said to her 'choose' intending divorce, and she chose in her sitting, she becomes separated by one divorce) because the one given choice has the option of the sitting by consensus of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, as a silent consensus when some of them explicitly stated it. What is narrated of the opposition of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, was not established. Ibn al-Mundhir held to it for those who do not require it by his statement, peace be upon him, to Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her: 'Do not hasten until you consult your parents', which is weak because this choice was not the disputed one, which is that she effects divorce by herself, but rather that if she chooses herself, he divorces her, evidenced by His statement: {O Prophet, say to your wives: If you desire the worldly life, then come, I will give you enjoyment and release you with a good release} [Al-Ahzab:28]. And he responded in al-Mi'raj that he, peace be upon him, gave her the option, up to the limit of consulting her parents, not absolutely, and our discussion is about the absolute. And because it is a tamlik (grant of ownership) of the act from her, since she is acting for herself, and it is confined to that. And it was objected regarding it being a tamlik from her: how can it be considered a tamlik while his ownership remains? And a single thing is impossible to be entirely owned by two persons? And he answered in al-Kafi that it is a tamlik of the occurrence (iq'a), not a tamlik of the substance, so before the occurrence his ownership remains. And it was objected regarding her acting for herself: if he appointed him to discharge himself from debt, he would be an agent, evidenced by the validity of his revocation before the discharge, even though the debtor acts for himself; and his answer and what is in it will come in the chapter of will (mashi'a). And the statement of al-Zayla'i in Agency when he said: 'and the agency of the guarantor for property is invalid, he is an owner and not an agent' implies that revocation from him is not valid, but this is not correct, for it is explicitly stated in al-'Inayah and others that it is not confined to the sitting and revocation from it is valid. And in al-'Inayah, tamlik is the legal empowerment over a place. And disposition, and agency is empowerment over disposition, so this doubt is repelled. But there is consideration: tamlik is the legal empowerment over the very disposition from the beginning, and agency is the legal empowerment over the very disposition not from the beginning, as is indicated in Fath al-Qadir at the beginning of the book of sale, and this is correct. Because there is no meaning to empowerment over the place except by considering disposition in it. And in al-Mi'raj, tamlik does not necessitate the invalidity of revocation, because it is contested by gift (hiba), for it is a tamlik and revocation is valid, but it is a tamlik that differs from other tamliks in that it remains beyond the sitting if she is absent, and it does not depend on acceptance because she divorces herself after the delegation, and it is (in terms of) incomplete tamlik conditioned by intention because it is from kinayat (allusive words), and the circumstantial indication (dalalat al-hal) stands in its place in judicial matters (qada) not in religious (diyana), and the indication is discussion of divorce or anger. And we have presented that it is purely for answer, and the saying is his with the oath in the absence of intention or indication, and her evidence is accepted to establish anger or discussion, not intention, unless it is established upon his admission to it, as mentioned by al-Walwaliji. And if he is not believed in court, she is not permitted to stay with him except with a new marriage because she is like a judge. And he only omitted mentioning the indication here due to knowledge from what he presented earlier in the chapter on kinayat. And he intended by 'intention of divorce' the intention of delegation, and he restricted it to the sitting because if she left it or began another action, her option becomes void, as we will mention. And he benefited by mentioning 'her sitting' that his sitting is not considered; so if he gave her choice then he stood up, her option does not become void, unlike her standing up, as in al-Bada'i'. And the truth is what is in al-Dhakhira and Jami' al-Fusulayn: it is a tamlik that contains the meaning of suspension (ta'liq), so because it is a tamlik...
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq). It begins by categorizing types of divorce by someone other than the husband: tafwid (delegation), tawkil (agency), and risalah (message). Tafwid to the wife is done with words of choice (takhyir), command by hand (amr bil-yad), or will (mashi'a). The primary example is when the husband says 'Ikhtari' (choose) intending divorce, and the wife chooses in the same majlis (sitting). This effects one ba'in divorce (one irrevocable separation). The proof is the silent consensus (ijma sukuti) of the Companions that the wife has the option of the sitting (khiyar al-majlis). The narration of Ali's opposition is not established. The commentary then defends the ruling against objections, including the Hadith to Aisha (which is weak). The key legal reasoning is that tafwid is tamlik (grant of ownership) of the divorce to the wife, not tawkil (agency). This distinction has practical consequences: in tamlik, the husband cannot revoke his delegation once the wife chooses, whereas in tawkil he could. The text addresses objections regarding the impossibility of two owners and the nature of acting for oneself, concluding that tafwid is a tamlik that contains the meaning of suspension (ta'liq), making it effective upon the wife's choice.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwīḍ): Delegation by the husband to the wife of the right to divorce herself.
تخيير (takhyīr): The husband saying 'ikhtari' (choose) to the wife, giving her the option to divorce.
خيار المجلس (khiyār al-majlis): The option of the sitting: the wife must choose in the same sitting as the tafwid for it to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A specific verse in the Quran.
B) A weak hadith from Aisha.
C) The silent consensus of the Companions.
D) Qiyas on the contract of sale.

Key Takeaway
When the husband says 'choose' intending divorce, the wife's immediate choice in the same sitting effects one irrevocable divorce, based on the Companions' consensus.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
10 min
Tafwid: Tamlik vs Tawkil and the Objections
Defends tamlik view of tafwid with objections and responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tamlik and tawkil in tafwid and explain the practical consequence regarding the husband's ability to revoke.

Core Idea
Tafwid is tamlik (grant of ownership) of the divorce to the wife, not tawkil (agency); thus the husband cannot revoke after the wife's choice.

After establishing the basic ruling, the text delves into the legal nature of tafwid. The key controversy is whether it is tamlik (grant of ownership) or tawkil (agency). This distinction has a direct practical consequence: can the husband revoke his delegation after the wife chooses? The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, holds that it is tamlik, meaning the husband cannot revoke. This lesson explores the objections raised against this view and the responses that confirm the tamlik position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Tafwid is tamlik: the husband grants ownership of the act of divorce to the wife. She is acting for herself, not as his agent. Therefore, once she chooses, the divorce is effective and the husband cannot revoke.
Tamlik here is of the act (iq'a), not the substance of marriage.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Some later Hanafi scholars (and possibly others) argue that tafwid is tawkil (agency), because the wife acts as the husband's representative. They reason that if it were tamlik, the wife would own the divorce, but the husband also retains ownership, which seems contradictory.
Also, analogy with ibra' (discharge) where the debtor acts for himself yet is an agent.
3
Examine the Hanafi responses to objections
Objection 1: A single thing cannot be owned by two persons. Response: It is tamlik of the occurrence (iq'a), not the substance; the husband retains ownership until she exercises the right. Objection 2: In ibra', the debtor acting for himself is an agent. Response: Tafwid is different; it is a special tamlik that is not purely agency.
The text also distinguishes tamlik as 'legal empowerment over the very disposition from the beginning' while tawkil is 'empowerment over the disposition not from the beginning'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under tamlik, the husband cannot revoke after the wife's choice; under tawkil, he can. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is tamlik, so revocation is invalid.
Also, in tamlik, the wife's option remains beyond the sitting if she is absent, and acceptance is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب تفويض الطلاق
لما فرغ من بيان ما يوقعه الزوج بنفسه صريحاً وكناية شرع فيما يوقعه غيره بإذنه وهو ثلاثة أنواع : تفويض وتوكيل ورسالة والتفويض إليها يكون بلفظ التخيير والأمر باليد والمشيئة، وقدم الأول لثبوته بصريح الدليل قوله : (ولو قال لها اختاري ينوي الطلاق فاختارت في مجلسها بانت بواحدة) لأن المخيرة لها خيار المجلس بإجماع الصحابة رضي الله عنهم إجماعاً سكوتياً عند تصريح بعضهم، وما نقل من خلاف علي رضي الله عنه لم يثبت، وتمسك ابن المنذر لمن لم يشترطه بقوله عليه السلام لعائشة رضي الله عنها «لا تعجلي حتى تستأمري أبويك ضعيف لأن هذا التخيير لم يكن المتنازع فيه وهو أن توقع بنفسها بل على أنها إن اختارت نفسها طلقها بدليل قوله تعالى فتعالين أمتعكن وأسرحكن سراحا جميلا [الأحزاب: ٢٨] وأجاب في المعراج بأنه عليه السلام جعل لها الخيار، إلى غاية استشارة أبويها لا مطلقاً وكلامنا في المطلق ا هـ . ولأنه تمليك الفعل منها لكونها عاملة لنفسها وهو يقتصر عليه وأورد على أنه تمليك منها أنه كيف يعتبر تمليكاً مع بقاء ملكه والشيء الواحد يستحيل أن يكون كله مملوكاً لشخصين؟ وأجاب في الكافي بأنه تمليك الإيقاع لا تمليك العين فقبل الإيقاع بقي ملكه ا هـ . وأورد على كونها عاملة لنفسها لو وكله بإبراء نفسه كان وكيلاً بدليل صحة رجوعه قبل الإبراء مع أن المديون عامل لنفسه، وسيأتي جوابه وما فيه في فصل المشيئة وقول الزيلعي في الوكالة عند قوله وبطل توكيل الكفيل بمال إنه مالك وليس بوكيل» يقتضي أن لا يصح الرجوع عنه ليس بصحيح فقد صرح في العناية وغيرها أنه لا يتقيد بالمجلس ويصح الرجوع عنه وفي العناية أن التمليك هو الإقدار الشرعي على محل
التصرف والتوكيل الإقدار على التصرف فاندفعت هذه الشبهة ا هـ . وفيه نظر لأن التمليك الإقدار الشرعي على نفس التصرف ابتداء، والتوكيل الإقدار الشرعي على نفس التصرف لا ابتداء كما أشار إليه في فتح القدير في أول كتاب البيع وهو الحق، لأنه لا معنى للإقرار على المحل إلا باعتبار التصرف فيه. وفي المعراج لا يلزم من التمليك عدم صحة الرجوع لانتقاضه بالهبة فإنها تمليك ويصح الرجوع لكنه تمليك يخالف سائر التمليكات من حيث إنه يبقى إلى ما وراء المجلس إذا كانت غائبة ولا يتوقف على القبول لكونها تطلق نفسها بعد التفويض وهو بعدم تمام التمليك قيد بالنية لأنه من الكنايات ودلالة الحال قائمة مقامها قضاء لا ديانة، والدلالة مذاكرة الطلاق أو الغضب، وقدمنا أنه مما تمحض للجواب والقول قوله مع اليمين في عدم النية أو الدلالة وتقبل بينتها على إثبات الغضب أو المذاكرة لا على النية إلا إذا قامت على إقراره بها كما ذكره الولوالجي. وإذا لم يصدق قضاء لا يسعها الإقامة معه إلا بنكاح مستقبل لأنها كالقاضي. وإنما ترك ذكر الدلالة هنا للعلم مما قدمه أول الكنايات. وأراد بنية الطلاق نية تفويضه وقيد بالمجلس لأنها لو قامت عنه أو أخذت في عمل آخر بطل خيارها كما سنذكره. وأفاد بذكر مجلسها أنه لا اعتبار بمجلسه، فلو خيرها ثم قام هو لم يبطل بخلاف قيامها كذا في البدائع. والحق ما في الذخيرة وفي جامع الفصولين أنه تمليك فيه معنى التعليق فلكونه تمليكاً
Chapter on Delegation of Divorce. When he finished explaining what the husband himself effects explicitly and allusively, he began on what someone else effects with his permission, which is three types: delegation, agency, and letter. Delegation to her is with the words of choice, command by hand, and will. He presented the first due to its being established by explicit proof: his statement: (And if he said to her 'choose' intending divorce, and she chose in her sitting, she becomes separated by one divorce) because the one given choice has the option of the sitting by consensus of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, as a silent consensus when some of them explicitly stated it. What is narrated of the opposition of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, was not established. Ibn al-Mundhir held to it for those who do not require it by his statement, peace be upon him, to Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her: 'Do not hasten until you consult your parents', which is weak because this choice was not the disputed one, which is that she effects divorce by herself, but rather that if she chooses herself, he divorces her, evidenced by His statement: {O Prophet, say to your wives: If you desire the worldly life, then come, I will give you enjoyment and release you with a good release} [Al-Ahzab:28]. And he responded in al-Mi'raj that he, peace be upon him, gave her the option, up to the limit of consulting her parents, not absolutely, and our discussion is about the absolute. And because it is a tamlik (grant of ownership) of the act from her, since she is acting for herself, and it is confined to that. And it was objected regarding it being a tamlik from her: how can it be considered a tamlik while his ownership remains? And a single thing is impossible to be entirely owned by two persons? And he answered in al-Kafi that it is a tamlik of the occurrence (iq'a), not a tamlik of the substance, so before the occurrence his ownership remains. And it was objected regarding her acting for herself: if he appointed him to discharge himself from debt, he would be an agent, evidenced by the validity of his revocation before the discharge, even though the debtor acts for himself; and his answer and what is in it will come in the chapter of will (mashi'a). And the statement of al-Zayla'i in Agency when he said: 'and the agency of the guarantor for property is invalid, he is an owner and not an agent' implies that revocation from him is not valid, but this is not correct, for it is explicitly stated in al-'Inayah and others that it is not confined to the sitting and revocation from it is valid. And in al-'Inayah, tamlik is the legal empowerment over a place. And disposition, and agency is empowerment over disposition, so this doubt is repelled. But there is consideration: tamlik is the legal empowerment over the very disposition from the beginning, and agency is the legal empowerment over the very disposition not from the beginning, as is indicated in Fath al-Qadir at the beginning of the book of sale, and this is correct. Because there is no meaning to empowerment over the place except by considering disposition in it. And in al-Mi'raj, tamlik does not necessitate the invalidity of revocation, because it is contested by gift (hiba), for it is a tamlik and revocation is valid, but it is a tamlik that differs from other tamliks in that it remains beyond the sitting if she is absent, and it does not depend on acceptance because she divorces herself after the delegation, and it is (in terms of) incomplete tamlik conditioned by intention because it is from kinayat (allusive words), and the circumstantial indication (dalalat al-hal) stands in its place in judicial matters (qada) not in religious (diyana), and the indication is discussion of divorce or anger. And we have presented that it is purely for answer, and the saying is his with the oath in the absence of intention or indication, and her evidence is accepted to establish anger or discussion, not intention, unless it is established upon his admission to it, as mentioned by al-Walwaliji. And if he is not believed in court, she is not permitted to stay with him except with a new marriage because she is like a judge. And he only omitted mentioning the indication here due to knowledge from what he presented earlier in the chapter on kinayat. And he intended by 'intention of divorce' the intention of delegation, and he restricted it to the sitting because if she left it or began another action, her option becomes void, as we will mention. And he benefited by mentioning 'her sitting' that his sitting is not considered; so if he gave her choice then he stood up, her option does not become void, unlike her standing up, as in al-Bada'i'. And the truth is what is in al-Dhakhira and Jami' al-Fusulayn: it is a tamlik that contains the meaning of suspension (ta'liq), so because it is a tamlik...
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq). It begins by categorizing types of divorce by someone other than the husband: tafwid (delegation), tawkil (agency), and risalah (message). Tafwid to the wife is done with words of choice (takhyir), command by hand (amr bil-yad), or will (mashi'a). The primary example is when the husband says 'Ikhtari' (choose) intending divorce, and the wife chooses in the same majlis (sitting). This effects one ba'in divorce (one irrevocable separation). The proof is the silent consensus (ijma sukuti) of the Companions that the wife has the option of the sitting (khiyar al-majlis). The narration of Ali's opposition is not established. The commentary then defends the ruling against objections, including the Hadith to Aisha (which is weak). The key legal reasoning is that tafwid is tamlik (grant of ownership) of the divorce to the wife, not tawkil (agency). This distinction has practical consequences: in tamlik, the husband cannot revoke his delegation once the wife chooses, whereas in tawkil he could. The text addresses objections regarding the impossibility of two owners and the nature of acting for oneself, concluding that tafwid is a tamlik that contains the meaning of suspension (ta'liq), making it effective upon the wife's choice.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlīk): Granting ownership of the act of divorce to the wife, so she can effect it herself.
توكيل (tawkil): Agency; the husband appointing the wife as his agent to divorce.
إيقاع (iq'a): Occurrence or effectuation of divorce; tamlik of iq'a means the wife owns the act of divorcing, not the marital bond.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a husband delegates divorce to his wife and she chooses in the sitting, can the husband later revoke the delegation?
A) Yes, because delegation is a type of agency.
B) No, because delegation is tamlik and the wife now owns the right.
C) Yes, but only if he revokes before she chooses.
D) No, but only if she has not yet chosen.

Key Takeaway
Tafwid is tamlik (grant of ownership) of the divorce to the wife, not tawkil (agency), so the husband cannot revoke once she chooses.

Tafwid is Tamlik, Not Tawkil: The Hanafi Distinction
Defines tafwid as tamlik with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tafwid, distinguish it from tawkil, and state the Hanafi position that it is tamlik with its rational proof.

Core Idea
Tafwid al-talaq is tamlik, not tawkil, because the wife receives legal capacity ab initio.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh regarding the delegation of divorce (tafwid). The author refutes the notion that tafwid is a form of agency, establishing it instead as a transfer of ownership (tamlik). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying rulings related to delegated divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions being compared
The author distinguishes between tamlik (giving ownership) and tawkil (agency). Both involve empowerment over an act, but differ in the nature of that empowerment.
2
Locate the core distinction
Tamlik gives legal capacity ab initio (from the start), while tawkil gives capacity only after appointment (not ab initio). This is the key criterion.
The author cites Fath al-Qadir for this definition.
3
Verify the Hanafi position and its rational proof
Tafwid is tamlik because the husband's delegation gives the wife immediate ownership of the right to divorce. The rational proof: there is no meaning to acknowledgment except by considering the act of tasarruf in it.
This settles the doubt that tafwid might be tawkil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التصرف والتوكيل الإقدار على التصرف فاندفعت هذه الشبهة ا هـ . وفيه نظر لأن التمليك الإقدار الشرعي على نفس التصرف ابتداء، والتوكيل الإقدار الشرعي على نفس التصرف لا ابتداء كما أشار إليه في فتح القدير في أول كتاب البيع وهو الحق، لأنه لا معنى للإقرار على المحل إلا باعتبار التصرف فيه.
Tasarruf and tawkil are [both] empowerment over tasarruf, so this doubt is repelled. But there is consideration: because tamlik is legal empowerment over the act itself ab initio, and tawkil is legal empowerment over the act itself not ab initio, as indicated in Fath al-Qadir at the beginning of the Book of Sale, and it is the truth, because there is no meaning to acknowledgment concerning the subject except by considering tasarruf in it.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of tafwid (delegation of divorce). The author clarifies that tafwid is tamlik (giving ownership) not tawkil (agency). The doubt that it might be tawkil is repelled because tamlik gives the wife legal capacity to act from the start, whereas tawkil only gives capacity to act later, after the appointment. The author cites Fath al-Qadir as authority and affirms the correct view as tamlik. This is a rational argument based on the meaning of empowerment.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Legal empowerment to act on one's own behalf from the start, like giving ownership.
توكيل (tawkil): Appointment of an agent, where the agent acts on behalf of the principal, not from the start.
تفويض (tafwid): Delegation of the right to divorce to the wife, which Hanafis classify as tamlik.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, is tafwid al-talaq (delegation of divorce) considered tamlik or tawkil?
A) Tamlik
B) Tawkil
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Tafwid is tamlik: the wife receives immediate ownership of the right to divorce, distinguishing it from agency.

Revocability and Intention in Tafwid
Expansion of rule on revocability of tafwid with intention requirements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on revocation of tafwid and explain the role of intention (niyya) and contextual evidence (dalalat al-hal) in qada' and diyana.

Core Idea
Tafwid is revocable like hibah; the wife's divorce is a kinayah requiring niyya, but context suffices in court.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on a rule from al-Mi'raj regarding the delegation of divorce (tafwid). It clarifies that the husband's grant of power is a tamlik that remains revocable, and addresses the crucial distinction between court rulings and religious obligation when intention is absent. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the law correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on revocation
The passage begins by establishing that tamlik does not bar revocation, using hibah as proof. State the ruling clearly: revocation of tafwid is valid.
The analogy to hibah is the key dalil.
2
Distinguish tafwid from ordinary tamlik
Note the special features: it extends beyond the council, does not require acceptance, and is incomplete until the wife acts. This explains why intention is needed.
These features make tafwid a unique tamlik.
3
Locate the requirement of intention
Since the wife's action is a kinayah, intention is needed. Identify the role of dalalat al-hal as a substitute in court (qada') but not in religion (diyana).
Contextual evidence like anger or divorce discussion suffices for court rulings.
4
Understand the evidentiary rules
The husband's word with oath is accepted regarding lack of intention or context. The wife's testimony is limited to proving external context (anger, discussion), not his intention, unless she has proof of his admission.
If the husband is not believed in court, she must separate and can only remarry after a new marriage.
5
Synthesize the overall position
Combine the revocation ruling with the niyya and evidence rules to articulate the complete Hanafi position: tafwid is revocable; the wife's divorce is effective only with intention, but evidence of context can establish it in court.
The mufta bihi position is as stated by al-Walwaliji.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المعراج لا يلزم من التمليك عدم صحة الرجوع لانتقاضه بالهبة فإنها تمليك ويصح الرجوع لكنه تمليك يخالف سائر التمليكات من حيث إنه يبقى إلى ما وراء المجلس إذا كانت غائبة ولا يتوقف على القبول لكونها تطلق نفسها بعد التفويض وهو بعدم تمام التمليك قيد بالنية لأنه من الكنايات ودلالة الحال قائمة مقامها قضاء لا ديانة، والدلالة مذاكرة الطلاق أو الغضب، وقدمنا أنه مما تمحض للجواب والقول قوله مع اليمين في عدم النية أو الدلالة وتقبل بينتها على إثبات الغضب أو المذاكرة لا على النية إلا إذا قامت على إقراره بها كما ذكره الولوالجي. وإذا لم يصدق قضاء لا يسعها الإقامة معه إلا بنكاح مستقبل لأنها كالقاضي. وإنما ترك ذكر الدلالة هنا للعلم مما قدمه أول الكنايات.
And in al-Mi'raj: From tamlik it does not follow that revocation is invalid, because it is refuted by hibah (gift), for it is tamlik and revocation is valid. But it is a tamlik that differs from other tamliks in that it remains after the council if [the wife] is absent, and it does not depend on acceptance because she divorces herself after tafwid, and it is [considered] incomplete tamlik. It is qualified by intention because it is from the kinayat, and the contextual evidence takes its place in the court, not in religious duty. The evidence is discussion of divorce or anger. We have stated that it is purely for answering, and his statement [i.e., the husband's] with oath regarding lack of intention or evidence is accepted. Her testimony is accepted to prove anger or discussion, not intention, unless it is based on his admission, as mentioned by al-Walwaliji. And if he is not believed in court, she cannot reside with him except with a new marriage because she is like a judge. He only omitted mentioning the evidence here because it is known from what he presented earlier about kinayat.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings of tafwid as tamlik. First, it states that tamlik does not necessarily prevent revocation (ruju'), as seen in hibah where revocation is valid. However, tafwid is a special tamlik: it remains valid after the council if the wife is absent, does not require her acceptance, and is considered incomplete tamlik until she acts. The wife's act of divorcing is a kinayah (allusive expression), so intention (niyya) is needed, but contextual evidence (like fighting or anger) can substitute for intention in court, though not religiously. If the husband denies having such intention or context, his word is accepted with oath. The wife can testify to the external context (anger, discussion) but not to his intention, unless she has proof of his admission. If the husband is not believed in court, the wife must separate and can only remarry after a new marriage. The discussion of evidence is omitted here because it was covered earlier in the chapter on kinayat.

Key Terms
كناية (kinayah): An allusive expression that requires intention to be effective in talaq.
دلالة الحال (dalalat al-hal): Contextual evidence (e.g., anger, discussion of divorce) that can replace intention in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi law, can a husband revoke the delegation of divorce (tafwid) before the wife exercises her option?
A) Yes, revocation is valid
B) No, it is irrevocable
C) Only if the wife consents
D) Only in the presence of witnesses

Key Takeaway
Tafwid is a revocable delegation; the wife's divorce using it is a kinayah, so intention is needed but contextual evidence suffices in court.

The Council and the Wife's Option in Tafwid Divorce
Specifies that wife's option is limited to the council

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of the council for the wife's option in tafwid divorce and identify which actions void it.

Core Idea
Only the wife's leaving the council voids her option; the husband's departure does not.

This lesson examines the specific ruling governing the wife's option to divorce herself when delegated by her husband. The passage clarifies that this right is temporally and spatially confined to the council (majlis) where the delegation occurred. Understanding this condition is crucial for correctly applying the rules of tafwid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the husband delegating divorce to his wife (tafwid al-talaq). The ruling is that the wife has an option (khayar) to accept or reject, but this option is conditional on remaining in the council.
2
Determine the role of the council
The council is the time and place where the delegation is made. The option is only active during this council; it does not extend beyond.
3
Distinguish between husband's and wife's actions
Only the wife's standing up or engaging in another action voids her option. The husband's standing up does not affect it.
The text explicitly says 'his council is not considered'
4
Consequence of leaving or engaging in another action
If the wife leaves the council or starts another action (like talking on phone, eating), her option becomes void immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بنية الطلاق نية تفويضه وقيد بالمجلس لأنها لو قامت عنه أو أخذت في عمل آخر بطل خيارها كما سنذكره. وأفاد بذكر مجلسها أنه لا اعتبار بمجلسه، فلو خيرها ثم قام هو لم يبطل بخلاف قيامها كذا في البدائع.
And he meant by 'intention of divorce' the intention of delegating it, and it is qualified by the council because if she leaves it or engages in another action, her option becomes void, as we will mention. And by mentioning 'her council' it indicates that his council is not considered; so if he delegated her then he stood up, it does not void [her option], unlike her standing up. Thus in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage explains that the wife's option to divorce under tafwid is limited to the council (majlis) where the delegation occurred. If she stands up from that council or starts another action, her option is voided. Only her standing up matters, not the husband's. So if the husband stands up, her option remains. This is based on al-Bada'i.

Key Terms
مجلس (majlis): The council or gathering where the delegation is made; the wife's option is limited to this session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband delegates divorce to his wife and then stands up, does the wife's option become void?
A) Yes, it becomes void
B) No, it remains
C) Only if she also stands
D) Only if he leaves the room

Key Takeaway
The wife's option in tafwid is confined to the council; only her departure or engagement in another activity voids it.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
6 min
Delegation with 'Mata Shi'ta' and the Absent Wife
Rulings on how different phrasings affect the council limitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between absolute delegation and time-bound delegation, and apply the rule that 'mata shi'ta' removes council limitation.

Core Idea
Mata shi’ta gives perpetual option; absent wife’s council is when she learns.

In delegating divorce to his wife, a husband may use phrases that either confine her option to the immediate council or extend it. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq explains key scenarios: the effect of adding 'whenever you wish', and the rule when the wife is absent. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi law in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Without qualification, 'ikhtari' limits the option to the council. Recognize this as the baseline.
The default is council-limited unless wording indicates extension.
2
Recognize the exception for 'mata shi'ta'
Adding 'mata shi'ta' (whenever you wish) removes the council limitation. The option continues indefinitely until revoked.
3
Apply the absent wife rule
If the wife is absent at delegation, her council is the moment she learns (majlis al-'ilm). The option period starts from that knowledge, not the husband's utterance.
This protects her right even if she hears later.
4
Understand time-bound delegations
If the husband says 'today', and she learns after the day passes, the option is void. The time limit is strict.
Similar logic applies to any specified duration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار باقتصاره على التخيير إلى أنه لو زاد متى شئت فإنه لا يتقيد بالمجلس فهو لها فيه وبعده وبخطابها إلى أنه لو خيرها وهي غائبة اعتبر مجلس علمها. ولو قال جعلت لها أن تطلق نفسها اليوم اعتبر مجلس علمها في هذا اليوم، فلو مضى اليوم ثم علمت خرج الأمر من يدها، وكذا كل وقت قيد التفويض به وهي غائبة ولم تعلم حتى انقضى بطل خيارها ولو قال الزوج علمت في مجلس القول وأنكرت المرأة فالقول لها لأنها منكرة. كذا في المحيط : ولو قال لها اختاري رأس الشهر فلها الخيار في الليلة الأولى واليوم الأول من الشهر، ولو قال اختاري إذا قدم فلان وإذا أهل الهلال فلها الخيار ساعة يقدم أو أهل الهلال في المجلس، ولو قال اختاري اليوم واختاري عداً فهما خياران، ولو قال في اليوم وغد فهو خيار واحد. كذا في المحيط أيضاً.
And by his restriction to the absolute delegation, he indicated that if he added 'whenever you wish', then it is not restricted to the council; it is available to her during it and after it. And by addressing her, it is indicated that if he delegated her while she was absent, her council of knowledge is considered. If he said 'I have given her [the right] to divorce herself today', her council of knowledge on that day is considered; if the day passes and then she learns, the matter leaves her hand. Similarly, for every time he restricts the delegation to, and she is absent and does not know until it expires, her option becomes void. And if the husband says 'she knew in the council of speech' and the woman denies, the word is hers because she is the denier. Thus in al-Muhit. And if he said to her 'choose at the beginning of the month', she has the option on the first night and the first day of the month. If he said 'choose when Zayd arrives' or 'when the new moon appears', she has the option at the moment of arrival or appearance in the council. If he said 'choose today' and 'choose a number', then there are two options. If he said 'today and tomorrow', it is one option. Thus in al-Muhit as well.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage details how different phrasings affect whether the wife's option is limited to the council. If the husband says 'choose whenever you wish' (ikhtari mata shi'ta), the option is not restricted to the council; it remains for the future. If the wife is absent at the time of delegation, her council of knowledge (meeting where she learns) is considered. If the husband restricts to a specific time (e.g., 'today'), and she learns after that time, the option is lost. If there is a dispute over whether she knew in the council, her word is accepted. Various examples: 'choose at the beginning of the month' gives option on the first night and day; 'choose when Zayd arrives' gives option at the moment of arrival, but only in the council? (the text says 'in the council', meaning the moment of arrival is like a council? Actually it says 'in the council', meaning she must choose immediately at the time of arrival, within that same gathering? The text says: 'falaha al-khiyar sa'ata yaqdamu aw ahl al-hilal fi al-majlis' – so she has the option at the hour of arrival or appearance, in the council. So the option is immediate, not extended. If he says 'choose today' and 'choose a number', there are two distinct options. If he says 'today and tomorrow', it is a single option covering both days.

Key Terms
مجلس العلم (majlis al-'ilm): The meeting where the wife learns of the delegation; considered her council if she was absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'I delegate divorce to you whenever you wish', is the wife's option limited to the council?
A) Yes, only in the council
B) No, it extends beyond the council
C) Only until the end of the day
D) Only if she accepts immediately

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'mata shi'ta' removes the council limitation; absent wife's option begins when she learns.
